Famous American Banker Talks About Europe Not Being at War, Impressions Gained from Traveling in Europe and Africa

(New York) Famous American banker Raymond, who traveled to Europe and Africa for ten weeks, returned here today and told reporters that he did not think there was a danger of a major war in Europe, because 95% of the people in all countries did not want war. Therefore, although democratic politics have suffered a major setback, those who rule Europe still do not dare to recklessly drive people who do not want war to the battlefield. According to reports, Mr. Lai is a shareholder of Morgan Bank. Shareholders of the bank have rarely spoken publicly in the past. Mr. Lai's remarks are considered very important by financial observers. (21st National News Agency Telegram)

Anti-Russian United Front, Hungarian Regent Asks Hitler, and Will Meet with Mussolini. Germany Claims Russia is Making Military Preparations

Hungarian Capital: Regent Horthy recently went hunting in Tyrol, Austria. He also visited German leader Hitler in Berchtesgaden, Germany (in Bavaria). According to political figures, the Regent's trip was purely a private visit and had no other meaning. According to well-informed sources, the Austrian army will soon hold large-scale exercises in Upper Austria and Carinthia. Regent Horthy will attend the exercises and will meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini at that time. (22nd Havas Agency Telegram)

(Vienna) The sudden visit of Hungarian Regent Horthy to German leader Hitler in Berchtesgaden, Germany, has surprised political figures here. They all believe that Horthy's trip is not just an ordinary visit. The most important issue he discussed with Hitler was the Soviet Union. It is said that after Horthy returns to Austria, he will also meet with President Miklas and Chancellor Schuschnigg. In addition, Italian North African Libya Governor Balbo is now in Austria and visited the local aircraft factory in Linz. This matter also seems to be related to Horthy's travels in Austria and Germany. (22nd Havas Agency Telegram)

Shipyards all over Soviet Russia are building warships day and night. (22nd National Telegram)

(Tokyo) As of the 22nd, the budget estimates for the next year's budget of each province, except for the army's budget and a part of the budget of the Ministry of Finance and other provinces, have been submitted to the Budget Bureau of the Ministry of Finance. (Tokyo) Japan's naval air force will be based on the second supplementary plan in October, and the opening of the Kanazawa (Yokohama) and Zhenhai (Korea) naval air base will be the last. However, the established plan is mainly based on the international situation from the past and considers the recent international situation. However, for Japan, which is surrounded by the sea on all sides, the air defense array on the sea and in the sky cannot be said to be sufficient. Therefore, the naval authorities have established a new air force expansion plan to ensure complete security, and the initial year's expenses have been included in the next year's budget submitted to the Ministry of Finance. However, what should be noted is that the new air force expansion plan is different from the established plan. Contrary to the previous focus on the increase of air squadrons and other general facilities, the future will focus on the training of passengers and the improvement of the performance of aircraft. The above decision is not within the bureau's authority. The bureau recently received a letter from the Director of the Madrid Postal and Telegraph Bureau, stating that all wired or wireless telegrams sent from Spain to other countries or from other countries to Spain can only be received and sent in designated telegraph offices within the country. Soviet Union Strengthens Naval Power; Aims to Resist Japanese and German Aggression; Special Attention Paid to the Defense of Vladivostok

Moscow Correspondence - After the Soviet Revolution, the expansion of land and air forces was pursued vigorously, but the strengthening of naval power lagged far behind. By 1927, when the construction of land and air forces had achieved some success, a supplementary plan was established. According to a statement by the Minister of the Navy in May 1929, "In the past two years, the Red Navy has been preparing for reorganization, disposing of six obsolete ships and building ten new ones, increasing its strength by a total of 13,000 tons." Since then, the Soviet Union has worked even harder to expand and reorganize, and today it has entered a period of construction. According to a report by Tukhachevsky, Deputy Chairman of the People's Commissariat of Defense, at the Central Executive Committee meeting earlier this year, "The Soviet Union's traditional shipbuilding policy has focused on submarines. This policy will be changed in the future to cover other types of ships. The Soviet Navy's budget has traditionally accounted for only 12% of the total defense budget, but it will be greatly increased in the future, and expansion will be carried out at the highest speed."

Red Fleet Deployment - The fleet is divided into five squadrons: Baltic, Black Sea, Caspian Sea, Pacific, and Amur River, stationed in Leningrad, Kronstadt, Vladivostok, Posiet Bay, Sevastopol, Arkhangelsk, Khabarovsk, Nikolaevsk, and their formations are as follows: (1) The Baltic Fleet has three battleships (old-style converted) of 22,000 tons each, with twelve 30cm guns, and a speed of 22 knots; one training ship of 11,900 tons; one cruiser of 6,800 tons; two gunboats, one of 1,700 tons and one of 1,300 tons; twelve large destroyers of 1,300 tons; three small destroyers of 600 tons; seventeen torpedo boats; about fifty submarines of 1,000 tons or 800 tons; two submarine tenders of about 3,000 tons; and several other auxiliary ships. (2) The Black Sea Fleet has two battleships (old-style converted), one of 23,000 tons with twelve 30cm guns and a speed of 23 knots, and one of 11,000 tons with four 30cm guns; three cruisers, one of 7,600 tons with four 30cm guns and a speed of 33 knots, and two of 6,800 tons each with fifteen 13cm guns and a speed of 26 knots; one cruiser of 6,800 tons with fourteen 13cm guns and a speed of 23 knots; seven large destroyers of about 1,200 tons with a speed of 33 knots; twenty-two small destroyers of about 400 tons; three torpedo boats of about 400 tons; about twenty submarines of 1,000 tons or 800 tons; one submarine tender of 3,000 tons; and several other auxiliary ships. (3) The Caspian Sea Fleet has two gunboats of 600 tons and six torpedo boats of 580 tons. (4) The Far East Fleet (i.e., the Pacific Fleet) has about forty submarines of 1,000 tons or 400 tons; five destroyers of about 800 tons; dozens of high-speed submarine chasers; about fifteen auxiliary cruisers; and four icebreakers. (5) The Amur River Fleet has ten large gunboats of 1,000 tons with several 15cm or 12cm guns; seven small gunboats of 350 tons or 200 tons with two 8cm guns; and about thirty motorboats of 30 tons or 10 tons.

Lessons of the Russo-Japanese War - The Soviet government, mindful of the disastrous defeat of the Imperial Russian fleet in the Russo-Japanese War, is paying particular attention to the strength of the fleet in Vladivostok, which faces Japan across the sea, to control the Tsushima Strait and other areas. In addition to the fifty newly completed, state-of-the-art submarines patrolling the coast of the port, high-speed torpedo boats of 700 tons capable of traveling at 40 knots are also being built to strengthen the defense of Vladivostok in the future. The port has recently established a fully equipped weapons factory and shipyard, and work is proceeding very actively. According to investigations, the Soviet Union is currently building one aircraft carrier of 7,600 tons, two Class A cruisers of 15,200 tons, four Class B cruisers of 20,000 tons, and six submarines of 5,700 tons, totaling thirteen ships of 48,500 tons. All of this is aimed at Japan and Germany to prevent aggression. (Special Dispatch from the China United News Agency)

An Overview of the Italian Labor Situation

— By Zhu Xuefan

Since the Fascist Party's march on Rome on October 28, 1922, and Mussolini's assumption of power in Italy, Mussolini has wielded a resolute hand, implementing an autocratic system. Over the past fourteen years, sweeping changes have been made in party and government affairs, economic reforms have been introduced, and social construction has been actively promoted. The remarkable achievements have been universally recognized. As for labor policies, they have greatly developed under Fascist rule. During my stay in Italy, I made a special effort to investigate the labor situation and provide a brief overview of my findings for the reference of those in China engaged in the labor movement.

(1) Labor Policy Before 1922, factory production in Italy was not very developed. Workers were often incited and exploited by the Communist Party, engaging in strikes and demonstrations to carry out destructive activities. This led to an increase in worker unemployment and hardship in their livelihoods, which had a profound impact and was detrimental to the security of the nation and society. After Mussolini came to power, he promulgated the Labor Charter (勞働大戀章), under the principle of labor-management cooperation and mutual assistance, working together to develop production. Factories were prohibited from using closures as a means of dealing with workers, and workers were prohibited from using strikes as a form of coercion. At the same time, labor contracts were established, stipulating minimum wages, working hours, rest periods, various holidays, and so on. Both labor and management were required to strictly comply, and the government would punish either party that violated the Labor Charter. As a result, labor disputes were drastically reduced, not only ensuring workers' livelihoods but also generally increasing factory production.

(2) Labor Organizations Currently, there are 2,204,275 organized workers in Italy, divided into 22 industries, all under the jurisdiction of the National Confederation of Industrial Unions. There are provincial federations in each province and county federations in each county. The National Confederation has a chairman who leads the national labor movement. The current chairman is Tullio Cianetli, who also serves as a member of the Grand Council. Each provincial federation has a provincial chairman, and each county federation has a county chairman, all appointed by the higher levels. Each factory has a representative, elected by the workers. The National Confederation is the only organization leading the workers. Its main tasks include representing workers in resolving labor disputes, negotiating contracts, and creating worker welfare programs. However, the Confederation must be guided by the "Ministry of Corporations" (行業合作部), Ministry Gi Co-operation, which also guides the Confederation of Industrial Employers. Therefore, there is a real connection between labor and management.

(3) Worker Life Worker life is currently relatively stable, with a 48-hour work week and one day of rest per week. Wages for night work are higher than those for day work. Workers mostly spend their leisure time engaging in entertainment at clubs. These clubs are jointly operated by the Party and the factories and offer various sports, music, fencing, travel, swimming, rowing, and foreign language courses. Therefore, I believe that the lives of foreign workers are not that different from those of Chinese workers. Foreign workers emphasize exercise and outdoor travel, while Chinese workers mostly stay indoors or visit entertainment venues during their leisure time. As a result, foreign workers are physically fit and mentally alert. On the contrary, this is true not only of workers in our country but also of ordinary people, which is a cause for concern.

(4) Labor Courts If labor and management encounter disputes, the National Confederation of Industrial Workers first conducts an investigation. If no resolution is reached, the matter is submitted to the Labor Court for adjudication. The Labor Court is composed of one employer representative, one worker representative, one expert, one judge, and two jury members. The Court adopts a fair attitude towards the cases presented and adjudicates them based on the principles of the Labor Charter. After the adjudication, both parties must strictly comply. Therefore, when labor disputes arise, they are resolved very quickly, and the effectiveness is evident. In 1935, there were only 120 labor disputes in Italy, which shows the general cooperation between labor and management.

(5) Employment Services A national employment service is established, with branch offices in each province, under the leadership of the Ministry of Corporations. Unemployed workers can register their age, skills, experience, and family situation with the local employment service. Employers must hire workers through the employment service and are not allowed to recruit workers on their own. This method is stipulated by law, and employers who do not comply will be fined from 50 lire to 3,000 lire (one lire is equivalent to one-fifth of Chinese legal currency). According to statistics from the Rome Employment Service branch, in April 1936, there were 10,957 unemployed men and 599 unemployed women, totaling 11,556 people. The number of people placed in jobs by the service was 6,753 men and 523 women, totaling 7,176 people.

(6) Labor Insurance Before 1922, due to the underdeveloped state of labor insurance, workers suffered greatly when they encountered unemployment, illness, disability, and other accidents. After Mussolini came to power, he actively promoted the labor insurance system. In recent years, its effectiveness has become apparent. There are now state-run and privately run insurance bureaus specializing in labor insurance. Privately run insurance bureaus must be guided by the Ministry of Corporations and the Ministry of Finance. As for the types of labor insurance, they include unemployment insurance, tuberculosis insurance, old age and disability insurance, expanded maternity insurance (for female workers), and accident insurance. Except for accident insurance premiums, which are fully borne by the factory owners, all other types of insurance premiums are borne equally by labor and management. Taking unemployment insurance as an example, according to statistics from 1934, insurance premium income was 120,222,000 lire, and subsidy expenditure was 101,384,000 lire. As for the tuberculosis insurance bureau, its facilities and arrangements are very thorough. There are currently 12 large-scale hospitals with 22,000 beds. Therefore, Italians who regularly insure themselves with various types of insurance can be free from worries about their lives and afterlives.

The above is a general overview of the current labor situation in Italy, and it is not possible to cover all the details. As for the issue of labor training, it falls within the scope of the entire Italian youth training program, which I will discuss in a separate article. Written on the 15th day of the 7th month of the 25th year [of the Republic], at a hotel in Germany.

Implementation of Land Tax Reform in Fujian Province; Deadline of Eight Months for Completion

Fuzhou Correspondence: Fujian Province's land tax has always lacked standards, and the resulting malpractices have not only made the government's treasury revenue uncertain, but also caused considerable suffering to the people due to inequality. Currently, the government's finances rely primarily on special business taxes, followed by slaughter taxes, livestock taxes, and broker taxes. According to the budget for the 24th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1935], land tax and poll tax were budgeted at over 2,670,000 yuan, but in reality, only 80%, or 2,000,000 yuan, was collected. Given the province's 61 counties and one city, the total land tax revenue is less than that of a single large county in Jiangsu or Zhejiang provinces. According to the recent survey by the provincial government's statistics office, the province has 17,700,400 mu of land. However, the fact that the average grain levy on the people is about 2.3 yuan per mu, including surcharges, proves the inequality of the people's burden: those who pay bear too heavy a burden, while many avoid payment altogether. Moreover, the county treasury clerks and runners engage in various malpractices, such as embezzlement and overcollection, which are also substantial. The government, deeply aware of the people's hardship and aiming to increase treasury revenue, has decided to implement land tax reform. The proposal was submitted by Finance Director Si Lie at the 86th meeting of the provincial government committee this month, and was approved, to ensure that no land is omitted, that the grain has a definite owner, that the people's burden is equal, and that the government's treasury revenue is certain, in order to promote political progress. Seven key points were decided: (1) Land tax reform is the most important central task of the 25th year [1936]; (2) The deadline is eight months for completion; (3) All counties are to issue orders to district office personnel, as well as Lianbao and Baojia heads, to fully mobilize and implement the reform; (4) The Land Administration Bureau is the responsible agency, responsible for all planning and implementation guidance; (5) The Finance Department is the supporting agency, responsible for all fundraising matters; (6) All departments of the provincial government are to assist in the success of this matter with all possible means; (7) All orders and announcements are to be issued in the name of the provincial government. After these key points were decided, all efforts were to be made to implement them separately, complete them on schedule, and issue new land deeds and tax payment certificates, so that the people can directly pay taxes. It was also decided that the collection of new grain would begin in the 26th year [1937]. Based on the province's 20 million mu of land, the total tax per mu, including surcharges, would be one yuan, which would reduce the people's tax burden by slightly less than one-third, while the government's treasury revenue would increase to more than 20 million yuan. Once this is accomplished, other similar harsh and miscellaneous taxes can gradually be abolished.

The Chinese Agricultural Society's Annual Meeting Held Yesterday in Zhenjiang; The Soil and Fertilizer Society of China Established Simultaneously

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The 19th annual meeting of the Chinese Agricultural Society and the society's 20th anniversary celebration were held yesterday morning (the 23rd) in Zhenjiang's Boxian Park. Over 120 members registered. Director Xu Tinghu of the Ministry of Industry. Dean Zou of the Agricultural College of Central University, Dean Liu Yunchou of the Agricultural College of Peking University. Dean Tong Shijin of Jiangxi Agricultural College. Tong Yumin of the Agricultural College of Zhejiang University. Li Yin of the Agricultural College of Sun Yat-sen University, as well as representatives from various agricultural agencies in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, and other provinces, participated. The meeting opened at 8:00 AM, with Chairman Liang Xi of the society's board of directors reporting on the preparations for the annual meeting. The 20th anniversary celebration was also held simultaneously. Considering the members' time and finances, the founding meeting of the Soil and Fertilizer Society of China and the annual meeting of the Chinese Phytopathological Society for the 25th year [1936] were also held simultaneously, as most of the members of both societies are also members of the Agricultural Society. Representatives Xu Tinghu of the Ministry of Industry, Luo Shishi of the Jiangsu Provincial Government. Xu Tigang of the Jiangsu Construction Department, and Professor Li Yin of the Agricultural College of Sun Yat-sen University, delivered speeches successively. The opening ceremony concluded at around 10:00 AM, followed by the reading of papers and discussion of society affairs in the afternoon.

Reading of Papers: The general meeting continued at 10:00 AM, chaired by Tang Qiyu, who reported that the number of papers received this year was greater than before, with extremely profound content and many novel inventions. A total of 108 papers were received, with the following distribution: Agronomy 20, Soil 25, Agricultural Economics 14, Forestry 13, Horticulture 12, Sericulture 12, Agricultural Chemistry 12, Pests and Diseases 7, Rural Society 1, Animal Husbandry 1, Other 1. Zeng Jikuan and others announced the paper titles, which lasted for over two hours.

Group Discussions: In the afternoon at 2:00 PM, agricultural issues were discussed in four groups: (1) Crop Improvement, moderated by Shen Zonghan and Feng Zefang; (2) Rural Economy, moderated by Huang Tong and Wu Taoren; (3) Sericulture, moderated by Sun Benzong and Jiang Shiqi; (4) Forestry, moderated by Li Yingong and Chen Rong. Members could choose a group to participate in the discussion, which concluded at 4:00 PM.

General Meeting: After the group discussions, a general meeting was held. First, Zou Shuwen and Chen Fangze reported on the progress of society affairs and the financial situation. Then, discussions began: (1) The location for the next meeting was tentatively set as Sichuan, Henan, or Jiangxi, to be decided by the next board of directors; (2) Regarding the case that the government should pay attention to agricultural candidates in the upcoming National Congress election, it was resolved that the general meeting would send a telegram to the National Government requesting that it prioritize genuine agricultural talents among the elected candidates in each province for the upcoming National Congress election; (3) Regarding the proposal that the Chinese Agricultural Society should establish a national agricultural discussion group to promote technical cooperation, it was resolved that the next board of directors would handle it; (4) Regarding the proposal to send a telegram to Li Bai in the name of the general meeting, urging him to immediately pull back from the precipice and make a final realization, after the proposal was discussed, nine electoral committee members were elected. Chen Rong, Zou Shuwen, Chen Fangji, Huang Gutong, Tang Qiyu, Wu Juenong, Chen Zhi, Liu Yunchou, and Hu Changzhi were elected as the electoral committee members for this session, and then the electoral committee members nominated thirty candidates for director, and used postal methods to send them to each member to elect ten formal directors.

Hosted Tours: All agenda items of the annual meeting were discussed and completed on the 23rd. On the 24th, the Jiangsu Construction Department hosted tours for the members to scenic spots, divided into three groups, with the following locations: Group 1: Jinshan, Beigushan, Meteorological Observatory, Ganlu Temple, Medical College, Jiaoshan; Group 2: Sibaidu Joint Sericulture Improvement Association, Southern Suburb Zhaoyin Temple, Helin Temple, Zhulin Temple, Huangshan, Beigushan, Medical College; Group 3: Maoshan, Provincial Forestry Experiment Station, Damao Palace, Sanmao Palace, Yin Palace. Xu Kangzu, Chen Zhi, Zhou Fei, and others served as guides respectively.

Another Dispatch: The Soil and Fertilizer Society of China held its founding meeting yesterday (the 23rd) in Zhenjiang. Most of the members are members of the Chinese Agricultural Society. Ma Shouzhen chaired the meeting, which approved the society's charter and elected Lan Mengjiu, Qian Peng, and Chen Fangji as electoral committee members, who then nominated candidates for director, and the members then elected them by mail.

Guangdong Provincial Government Approves Temporary Regulations Banning Gambling; Gambling Prohibition Committee to Be Established by End of Month; Gambling Prohibition to Begin September 1st

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangdong Provincial Government has recently been making great efforts to eradicate smoking and gambling, eliminate corruption, and maintain the reputation of the birthplace of the revolution. Therefore, at the provincial affairs meeting on the 19th, it was decided to ban smoking and gambling from September 1st. The task of banning smoking was assigned to the Anti-Smoking Bureau and the Finance Department to discuss the specific measures. As for the implementation of gambling prohibition, the Guangdong Provincial Gambling Prohibition Committee will be established first to take charge. The committee will consist of seven members, with Provincial Government Chairman Huang Musong appointed as the chairman of the Gambling Prohibition Committee, and Civil Affairs Director Wang Yingyu, Finance Director Song Ziliang, Fourth Route Army Commander Yu Hanmou, Chief of Staff of the Xingying [New Army] Chen Cheng, and High Court President Shi Yancheng as members. The committee is to be established by the end of this month and attached to the Provincial Government, with funding allocated from the provincial treasury. As for the gambling prohibition measures, the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments have drafted the Guangdong Provincial Temporary Regulations Banning Gambling, which were submitted to the second provincial affairs meeting on the 21st and amended and approved. The Guangdong Provincial Temporary Regulations Banning Gambling are recorded below: Article 1: The Guangdong Provincial Government hereby enacts these regulations for the purpose of permanently eradicating gambling throughout the province. Article 2: Any activity referred to as gambling, such as Fantan, Shanli, Puli, Eight Character Righteous Associations, Flower Associations, Mahjong, and all other types of gambling, involving wagering with property, shall be subject to these regulations. Article 3: Anyone who gambles with property shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to two years or a fine of up to one thousand yuan. Article 4: Anyone who engages in gambling as a profession shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to three years and may also be fined up to two thousand yuan. Article 5: Anyone who intends to profit from operating a gambling den shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to five years and may also be fined up to three thousand yuan. Article 6: Anyone who leases a building to someone for the purpose of operating a gambling business shall be fined up to four thousand yuan, and the building may also be confiscated. Article 7: Anyone who acts as an intermediary for the sale or purchase of Shanpu tickets, lottery tickets, or similar Shanpu tickets shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to two years or a fine of up to two thousand yuan. Article 8: Anyone who manufactures or sells gambling equipment shall be sentenced to detention for up to one month or a fine of up to five hundred yuan. Article 9: Local bullies and gentry who harbor gamblers shall be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for more than ten years. Article 10: Government officials who gamble with property shall be punished more severely in accordance with the provisions of Articles 3, 4, and 5. Those who harbor gamblers shall be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for more than ten years. Article 11: Gambling equipment and property at gambling tables or exchange counters, regardless of whether they belong to the offenders or not, shall be confiscated. Article 12: Anyone who reports gambling and leads to a successful arrest shall be rewarded with half of the confiscated property and fines. Article 13: Anyone who frames, slanders, or fabricates evidence to falsely accuse another person of violating these regulations shall be punished with the same penalty as the crime they accused the other person of. Article 14: Anyone who violates these regulations shall be handled by the county or city government in each county or city, and by the Public Security Bureau in the provincial capital, and reported to the provincial government and the Gambling Prohibition Committee for verification. Article 15: These regulations shall be implemented from September 1st, 25th year of the Republic [1936], and reported to the National Government for record. (August 22nd)

Gunfight Between Police and Bandits in Xiamen City

Xiamen Correspondence: An unprecedented fierce gunfight between police and bandits occurred in Xiamen City on the 21st. Recently, a series of robberies have occurred in Xiamen. In addition to the detective team, the Public Security Bureau has established a special task force, with Director Shen Jinkang concurrently serving as the director, to secretly track down bandits. On the morning of the 21st, Shen received a secret report from a task force member that the bandits Zhang Sichuan and others had recently robbed the homes of Zhu Xianting on Jiaowei Road, a certain family at No. 180 Xiameng, and the overseas Chinese merchant Chen Zhitang in Caopucheng. Today, they gathered at Huacheng Teahouse at No. 139 Xianfeng Camp to rob the wealthy Chen family in Fuyou Palace. The next day, they will gather at Zhongshan Park to rob the wealthy Wu family on Siming East Road, and then flee back to Haicheng. Based on the report, Shen immediately dispatched task force member Sun Shaokang to lead six capable detectives disguised to arrest them. Sure enough, four people were sitting around a table drinking tea in front of Huacheng. One was wearing a black Xiangyun gauze shirt and pants, one was wearing a white shirt and pants, and two were wearing white student uniforms. Sun pretended to be a cigarette buyer and entered the shop first. Special police officers Yang Shiren and Zhang Zhenwu also followed in. Once inside, Yang and Zhang unexpectedly grabbed a bandit each from behind. Unexpectedly, a bandit sitting nearby immediately drew a gun and fired. Yang was shot in the left forehead and fell to the ground. The two bandits broke free. At this time, detectives outside the shop also rushed in, and the bandits and police exchanged fire. Gunshots rang out everywhere, and bullets fell like rain. The black-clad bandit burst out the door and fled, but was shot and fell to the ground. The remaining three bandits fled to the road. Coincidentally, the Marine Corps barracks were across the street. More than ten soldiers heard the gunshots and came to assist. They encountered the three fleeing bandits and fired two volleys of shots into the air. The bandits fled, and the detectives chased after them, capturing two of the bandits. The remaining bandit escaped. Two Mauser pistols and one revolver were seized. The black-clad bandit was shot four times and died on the spot. Policeman Yang had a bullet lodged in his head, and blood flowed from his mouth and nose. He died of his injuries after being sent to the hospital for treatment. One captured bandit identified himself as Zhang Sichuan, and another identified himself as Gao Xu, also known as Ji Wenfang. They confessed that they were responsible for the robbery in Caopucheng. They were immediately detained for investigation.

Songjiang: Water Patrol Team Captures Bandits

He Dayou and Sun Rongsheng, both from Shaoxing, jointly founded Heshengji Shipping Company, specializing in transporting goods from Zhangkan, Luxiang, and Zhangze to Shanghai. Yesterday at noon, the ship set off from Shanghai loaded with many packages of flour, tea, sugar and other goods, worth several hundred yuan, and sailed to Songjiang. At around 9:00 PM, it arrived at Zhangze Port to wait for the tide and temporarily stopped. At around 11:00 PM, two Jiangbei boats suddenly approached the ship. More than ten people boarded the ship, led by two people each holding a pistol, and ordered the six crew members of Heshengji, including A-Quan, to be tied up. They looted the cargo and stole seven copies of freight manifests, over thirty silver dollars, fifteen thousand copper coins, and clothes. The bandit ships sailed eastward. The shipping company immediately went to Songjiang overnight to report to the water patrol team. After receiving the report, Captain Fei Gongxia immediately supervised the police officers and personally took the Yun Jian [Cloud Room] steamboat to pursue them. At 6:00 AM this morning, they saw two Jiangbei boats parked in Minhang Zhongchao Port, which were quite suspicious. As they were searching, a bandit swam away. The police officers also went into the water and caught him. They immediately found the stolen goods on the boat. The bandits Zhang Yaoqi, Wang Pengshi, Zhang Xiaonizi, Wang Dejin, Zhang Genbao, Zhang Qianshi, Lu Chenshi, Zhang Guiying, Chen A-si, and four children, along with the bandit boats and stolen goods, were brought back for interrogation. It is said that the two main bandits happened to land seven li away, so they escaped the net.

Wuxi: Giant Python Discovered in Meicun

There is a large abandoned tomb in the second district of the county, near Meicun Town, commonly known as Yantai Tomb. The tomb has a double-layered enclosure wall, but it is located in a remote and desolate area, rarely visited by people. Yesterday, villagers came to the city to report that a large python had been discovered on the upper part of the enclosure wall inside the tomb two days ago. It was over four zhang [approximately 13 meters] long, completely black, with a diameter of one chi [approximately 33 cm], and a head as big as a dou [approximately 10 liters], with bright, piercing eyes. At the time, a villager caught a glimpse of it and mistakenly thought it was a black wooden electric pole lying on the enclosure wall. When he returned to the tomb, he realized it was a giant python and was greatly frightened. He rushed to Meicun Town and told everyone he met. When the crowd went to see it, the snake had already disappeared. It is said that giant pythons have been discovered twice in the tomb in the past twenty or thirty years.

Nantong: Riverbank Collapse and Emergency Rescue

The riverbank in Tongyi [Nantong] has been collapsing more and more severely recently. The two hills of Huangni and Ma'an are about to fall into the river. The people of Yao Dong and various weirs [polders] have been automatically reinforcing the dikes to defend against the tide. The Construction Bureau is implementing an emergency project to reinforce the riverbank with stone, and the county government has allocated 17,000 yuan for this purpose.

Yangzhou: Huaiyang Garrison Command Moves to Yangzhou. The Huaiyang Garrison Command, originally stationed in Qingjiang, was ordered by the Ministry of Military Administration to move to Yangzhou for the convenience of military service. Commander Yang obeyed the order and sent personnel to Yangzhou to survey and select a location to station. They chose Wanshou Temple. The command's soldiers have already traveled south from Qingjiang yesterday. Commander Yang Tingya also arrived in Yangzhou at around 4:00 AM on the 22nd. Upon receiving the news, the Jiangdu Military Service District Command sent a delegation to welcome him into the city at the riverbank.

Pinghu: Major Disturbance at Jin Sinang Bridge

On the 17th, the Zhejiang Border Inspection Office found a passenger named Huang Jinlong carrying a handgun in a car on the Shanghai-Pinghu Road. He was sent to the county for interrogation. Huang confessed that his friends Lu A-Da and Lu A-Huai also had handguns and were currently in Jin Sinang Bridge Town. Therefore, the county supervisor led a detective team and brought Huang Jinlong as an informant to arrest them. They arrived at the town and found the Lu brothers gambling in a teahouse. They were immediately apprehended. As they were about to return to the city, they suddenly heard a noisy crowd approaching from afar. Before they had gone halfway, they heard shouts and were being chased by a crowd of about a hundred people. Fearing that they would be snatched away, they shot the Lu brothers. A-Huai was seriously injured and fell to the ground, and A-Da died on the spot. Huang Jinlong escaped in the chaos. The detective team, fearing for their lives, fled to the township head's office and telegraphed the county government. Upon receiving the report, County Magistrate Wang led armed police officers and telegraphed the garrison in Zhapu to rush to the scene. However, everyone had disappeared. The village head was also missing. The supervisors and others were unharmed. They then went to Lu A-Huai's house and arrested his wife, Mrs. So-and-so, and took her to the county.

Hangzhou: Continued Joint Operation on Jiangguang Road

The Jiang (shan)-Guang (feng) Highway on the Zhejiang-Jiangxi border is operated by the Highway Bureau in Zhejiang Province, while the Guangfeng Automobile Company operates the Jiangxi Province section. To facilitate passengers, both parties previously negotiated and signed a contract to operate joint passenger and freight transport, with a joint transport station at Xintangbian Station. Xiaoshan: Promising Cotton Harvest in the Eastern Region

The sandy and fertile soil of Guali, Nanyang, Dangshan, and other places in the eastern region of Xiaoshan is suitable for growing cotton. Every year, the harvest is transported and sold to other places in large quantities. The climate this summer has been favorable. If there are no special climate changes in the next half month, it is estimated that each mu can yield more than 200 jin. In addition, the American cotton planted in the cotton trial planting experiment zone is expected to be more abundant than in previous years.

Education Broadcasting Special Issue

Effective Methods for Preventing Rice Stem Borers, Aphids, and Locusts (Part 1)

— Wu Fuzhen, Dean of the College of Agriculture, Zhejiang University

There are many types of agricultural pests, among which the three most widespread and damaging are rice stem borers, aphids, and locusts. According to a survey by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station: In 1933, the loss of crops nationwide due to rice stem borers was valued at 14.7 million silver dollars; in 1934, the loss of cotton nationwide due to aphids was valued at 10 million silver dollars; in 1935, the loss of rice in Jiangsu Province alone due to rice stem borers was valued at 11 million silver dollars. Currently, our country is striving for self-sufficiency in food and cotton, so we must do our utmost to prevent and control the above three types of pests. Now, I will briefly discuss effective methods for preventing and controlling them:

(A) Rice Stem Borers

Rice stem borers are pests of rice. Their names vary greatly from place to place. Some places call them "floating insects," some call them "white stalk insects," and some call them "heart-drilling insects"... Different views lead to different names.

There are distinctions between the two-brood rice stem borer, the three-brood rice stem borer, and the large rice stem borer. The "two-brood" rice stem borer generally has two generations per year, so it is called the two-brood rice stem borer; the three-brood rice stem borer generally has three generations per year, so it is called the three-brood rice stem borer; although the large rice stem borer also has three generations per year, it is called the large rice stem borer because it is the largest of the three types of rice stem borers. Although their types are different, their life habits and damage are mostly similar, so the prevention and control methods are also roughly the same. Now, to save time, I will take the three-brood rice stem borer, which is the most damaging of the three, as a representative to explain.

(1) The Life Cycle of the Rice Stem Borer

The rice stem borer is an insect with complete metamorphosis. Its life cycle has four stages: egg, larva, pupa, and adult. The eggs are laid on the seedlings and rice leaves, in clusters of thirty or forty to over a hundred, arranged overlapping each other, covered with brownish-yellow scales, and appearing like half a soybean. The larvae that hatch from the eggs undergo more than a month, molting five times, before turning into pupae. After another five or six days, they turn into adults—the rice stem borer moths. This cycle of growth completes three generations in a year. The third generation of larvae, when the rice is mature and the weather is gradually getting colder, hides in the rice roots to overwinter. Then, in the middle and late May of the following year, when the weather gradually warms up and the seedlings grow, they pupate and turn into moths again, flying to the seedling fields and laying eggs on the seedling leaves. The larvae that hatch from the eggs bore into the seedling stems, causing the seedlings to turn yellow and die; this is the first generation. By mid-July, the second generation of larvae appears. At this time, the rice fields are often damaged by "dead heart rice," forming round clusters, the size of a farmer's bamboo hat, so farmers call it "bamboo hat blight." By mid-August, the third generation of larvae appears. At this time, the rice is in the heading stage, and the rice that is eaten by them becomes white spikes. Therefore, rice fields with and without rice stem borers are very easy to distinguish. The reproductive capacity of rice stem borers is very strong, which is why they are so damaging. Assuming that each rice stem borer moth lays one hundred eggs as a standard, and calculating half male and half female, by the third generation, it can reproduce to 250,000 rice stem borers. Therefore, if a few rice stem borer moths remain in the seedling fields in the spring, by autumn, only white spikes will be seen in the widespread rice fields.

(2) Effective Prevention and Control Methods for Rice Stem Borers

There are many methods for preventing and controlling rice stem borers. Now, I will talk about several effective and easy-to-implement methods:

(1) Egg Removal Egg removal means folding off and burning the egg masses laid by rice stem borer moths on seedling leaves or rice leaves. Egg removal can be carried out in three stages: The first stage is egg collection in seedling fields. However, egg collection in seedling fields is difficult to implement in the old-fashioned seedling fields of the Jiangnan area, where there are no walkways. Therefore, to collect eggs in seedling fields, it is necessary to first implement modern seedling fields. The method of modern seedling fields is to sow the rice seeds into four-foot-wide strips, with a one-foot-wide path between every two strips, so that people can walk when collecting eggs. When the seedlings grow to three or four inches high in early May, it is necessary to patrol the seedling fields, and if egg masses are found, they should be collected at any time. The egg collectors must bring a stick and a cloth bag, and on the sunny side, gently move the seedling leaves with the stick, watch carefully, and move forward slowly. When egg masses are seen, they should be collected into the cloth bag. After the collection is completed, they should be gathered and burned. Egg collection in seedling fields must be carried out at least once every three days. This work is very simple, as long as one has good eyesight and can walk in paddy fields, almost anyone can do it. However, children with moderate bodies and sharp eyes are particularly suitable for this work, and parents should make good use of them. Egg collection in seedling fields is inevitably missed, so when the second generation of egg masses occurs in mid-July and the third generation of egg masses occurs in early August, egg collection in the fields should be carried out, which is the second and third stages of egg collection. The method of egg collection in the fields is the same as that in the seedling fields, but the area is larger, the work is more time-consuming, and it must be done once a day.

(2) Larva Removal Rice stem borer larvae overwinter in the rice roots, as mentioned above, so the best way to remove larvae is to dig up the rice roots in winter and destroy them all. The larvae hidden in them can then be killed. There is no special method for digging up rice roots. After the rice is harvested and before the next crop is planted, use a hoe or spade to dig them up, and then choose the following methods for disposal:

(1) Stack the rice roots and river mud in layers, and then cover the surroundings with river mud. After the rice roots have rotted, they can be used as fertilizer.

(2) Dig a deep pit, bury the rice roots in the pit, and use them as fertilizer after they have rotted.

(3) Mix them with dry rice straw, pile them in the field, and set them on fire.

(4) Dry the rice roots and use them as fuel.

In addition to digging up rice roots to kill larvae, there is also a method of flooding and soaking. That is, in rice fields where no crops are planted and where water conservancy is very convenient, flood the fields so that the larvae hidden in the rice roots suffocate and die. The depth of the flooding should be appropriate to submerge the rice roots. The flooding period should be more than two months.

(3) Moth Removal The best way to remove moths is to do it during the seedling stage. On the one hand, use insect nets to catch and kill them; on the other hand, use the phototropic habits of rice stem borer moths to lure and kill them by lighting lamps next to the seedling fields. This lamp is called a moth-luring lamp. The installation is very simple. Usually, a tripod can be set up on the field ridge, with a strong kerosene lamp hanging on it. Place a round basin three feet in diameter directly below the lamp, fill the basin half full with water, and add a few drops of kerosene. The distance between the lamp and the basin should be about seven or eight inches, and the distance from the lamp to the ground should be about six feet. Turn on the lamp every night from 7:00 pm to 12:00 am. When the rice stem borer moths see the light, they will fly to the bottom of the lamp, fall into the water, and die from the oil. Usually, one lamp is lit per acre of field. If there are too many rice stem borer moths, the number of lamps should be increased appropriately to increase the effect.

If the above-mentioned methods of treating rice stem borers can be implemented step by step, then the damage from rice stem borers can definitely be eliminated. However, three points should also be noted:

Silk and Satin Industry Asks for Revision / Inspection Measures for Artificial Silk Fabrics

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association believes that the "Inspection and Clearance Measures for Domestically Produced Piece Goods Woven with Artificial Silk" promulgated by the Ministry of Finance are difficult to implement. It has telegraphed the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the association to request revisions, and each has sent representatives to Beijing to petition. It was fortunate to be granted relief and ordered the Inspector General of the Jianghai Customs to review and report. Now, it is learned that the association has not received approval after ten days. Recently, the Shanghai Post Office has allowed each household to mail one package of silk, limited to a value of 55 customs gold units (equivalent to 120 national currency), which has caused merchants from all over the country to gather in Shanghai, all hesitating and not daring to buy goods. However, there are 5,000 to 6,000 pieces of Ge Ti transported from Zhoucun, Shandong, to Shanghai every day. The association believes that the circulation of smuggled goods is like this, while the restrictions on legitimate goods are so severe. At the beginning of the autumn sales season, goods will soon become outdated. If relief is not provided, not only will losses be worrying, but also tens of millions of silk industry workers and merchants will be plunged into despair. Therefore, the association convened a special executive committee meeting yesterday and resolved to publicly recommend Chairman Luo Qinghua Fang to submit a document again to Beijing to continue waiting for instructions. It was learned that the Hangzhou Silk Industry Association also believes that the inspection measures are very difficult and has telegraphed the Hangzhou Customs Supervisor and the Customs Commissioner to request their review and transfer to seek relief, and has recorded the telegram and letter to ask the association to preside over the handling. The original text of the letter is recorded below:

To the Ministry of Finance, respectfully submitted: The association believes that the "Inspection and Clearance Measures for Domestically Produced Piece Goods Woven with Artificial Silk" promulgated by the Ministry of Finance are difficult to implement. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the association have sent representatives to petition in person, and the Ministry granted relief. After ten days, no approval has been received, which is deeply worrying. The Shanghai shipping industry has already been virtually suspended, and recently the post office has limited the delivery of silk goods to 55 customs gold units per household, with a price below 120 yuan in national currency. At the beginning of the autumn sales season, merchants from all over the country are gathering in Shanghai, hesitating due to transportation delays or not daring to buy goods. Goods will soon become outdated. Not only will losses be worrying, but also tens of millions of silk workers and merchants will be driven into despair. Looking ahead, we are terrified. The most painful thing is that the Ti Wan from Zhoucun, Shandong, can be sold smoothly without obstruction. According to reports, 5,000 to 6,000 pieces are transported to Shanghai every day for dumping at low prices. The circulation of smuggled goods is like this, while the restrictions on legitimate goods are so severe, which is not the original intention of the Ministry. According to the regulations of the post office, with a price limit of 120 yuan, each piece of Ti Ge produced in Shandong, which is only worth about 4 yuan in national currency, can be sent in batches of 30 pieces. As far as the flow of money is concerned, there is no more smuggling to be inspected. Under this situation, hundreds of thousands of silk merchants and machine households affiliated with the association in Hangzhou, Huzhou, Suzhou, Sheng, and other places are suffering deeply and hating the smooth sale of smuggled goods. The result of anti-smuggling has become the protection of smuggled goods and the destruction of domestic products. Thinking of this, we cannot help but feel sad and angry. Therefore, we are sending Chairman Luo Qinghua Qi again to submit a petition and continue to wait for instructions, lest we be eager to await orders. Respectfully submitted to Kong, Minister of the Ministry of Finance, Luo Qinghua, Chairman of the Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association.

Letter from the Hangzhou Association: Our association, etc., believes that the inspection and clearance measures set by the Ministry of Finance have various difficulties in implementation. On the 10th of this month, we telegraphed the Hangzhou Customs Supervisor and the Customs Commissioner to request a review and understanding. The original telegram is recorded below (omitted above). The Hangzhou Customs Bulletin No. 34 has been issued for the inspection and clearance measures for domestically produced piece goods woven with artificial silk or mixed with artificial silk, as stipulated by the Ministry of Finance, and is scheduled to be implemented within a limited time. Our association, etc., believes that the measures have many difficulties in relation to the actual situation of the silk industry in this city and have raised various difficult problems. We have sent representatives to visit in person, and it was reported that the case was submitted to the Ministry of Finance. All domestically produced piece goods woven with artificial silk or mixed with artificial silk within the Hangzhou Customs area, regardless of silk merchants, silk factories, or retail machine households, must be handled in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry, etc. After detailed discussion, we have not been able to implement the following difficult situations: (1) Regarding the machine households in this city, there are about 6,000 or more retail machine households in this city, which are completely family-run handicrafts. Today, they weave a piece and must sell it in the silk market, selling as they weave and selling locally without direct transportation and sales. Moreover, the raw materials of artificial silk they need are supplied by the local artificial silk shops, which are purchased from the initial artificial silk importers in small amounts and several times. It is impossible to obtain tax bills. This is one. (2) Regarding the silk merchants, there are no less than hundreds of shops in this city that operate silk sales, which can be said to be the center of the silk industry in Hangzhou. The domestically produced piece goods they sell are entirely purchased directly or indirectly from the retail machine households in this city and the interior. When they sell to other places, they cannot obtain the machine household's tax payment certificate and exchange for a license. This is two. (3) Regarding the machine households in the interior, such as Huashe Xiafangqiao in Shaoxing, etc., the domestically produced piece goods they weave are either carried to Hangzhou for sale by the machine households themselves, or purchased by silk merchants and transported to Hangzhou for sale. When they are shipped and distributed, they also have no way to obtain a certificate to exchange for a license. This is three. (4) Regarding the silk factories, since the economic panic tide, its impact on the development of the silk factories in this city has been very profound. Currently, there are no more than a few silk factories in this city that can be called silk factories. Before the machine households and silk merchants' license exchange methods are changed, the silk produced by the silk factories and the silk produced by the machine households will inevitably be difficult to distinguish. This is four. In short, the center of the largest output of silk piece goods in this city is tied to the retail machine households, and its silk merchants are the collective organization for its transportation and sales. Between the mutual relationship between these two, there are tens of thousands of difficulties in obtaining tax bills and exchanging for transportation licenses. At the same time, the Shanghai Silk Industry Association has a linked relationship with the situation of the silk industry in this city. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce has previously submitted a detailed report to the Ministry of Finance and sent representatives to Beijing to petition. The Ministry of Finance has been detailed and clear, and has allowed the Inspector General of Customs to review and provide relief measures. For the implementation date, the Ministry also ordered to consider the family situation. The difficulties of the silk industry in Hangzhou are detailed on the left and right, and we request that you review and approve them and quickly forward them to the Inspector General of Customs for review and relief measures, and request that the implementation be delayed before the relief measures are reviewed and determined, so as not to cause the entire industry to stop. We cannot help but wait eagerly for orders. Hangzhou Silk and Satin Industry Association, Electrical Silk Weaving Industry Association, bowed and sealed together, and should be informed, to hope that the platform will be integrated, Ho.

Legitimate Goods Transportation and Sales / Please Do Not Make Things Difficult / The City Chamber of Commerce Presents a Telegram to the Ministry of Finance

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, "Finance Minister Jian, on the 21st of this month, the anti-smuggling committee of the association held its sixth regular meeting. The director of the inspection team, Ti Yi, reported that since the government vigorously implemented anti-smuggling, although smuggled goods on Jianghai ships and road transportation have gradually disappeared, many traitors have changed the smuggled goods to be transported to the interior for sales by private boats, small ships, barges, or long-distance buses to avoid inspection. Anti-smuggling agencies in various places have not yet paid widespread attention. At present, due to anti-smuggling relations, legitimate goods are often transported and sold to various places, and they are often made difficult by inspectors, and are detained for no reason, hindering commerce. Please seek relief." It was unanimously agreed that the Ministry should issue an order to anti-smuggling agencies in various places to pay attention to the cargo transportation of private boats, small ships, highways, and buses, strictly prevent smuggled goods, and at the same time warn inspectors to facilitate the transportation and sale of legitimate goods and not to arbitrarily make things difficult. The discussion and decision were passed. We hereby telegraph the Ministry to review and implement it, which is convenient for the public. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce worships and supports.

It is the Beginning of the Autumn Flood Season / The Construction Department Surveys the Baoshan Seawall / The Dike Blocking Work at Shitangkou and Other Places Is Completed / The County Government Telegraphes the Province to Quickly Allocate Flood Prevention Funds

According to Dagong News Agency, after the collapse of the bank walls at Shitangkou outside Dongmen and Laoshidong in the Fifth District of the Baoshan Seawall, the county government not only quickly sought to block the breach by requisitioning labor, but also telegraphed the provincial government to allocate funds for prevention. Now the Construction Department has sent Chen Zhitian to the seawall for a survey, and has prepared a large number of sacks of sand and stone to fill the breaches. The details are recorded as follows by a reporter from Dagong News Agency:

The Breach Blocking Is Completed

Since the tail of the first hurricane in Shanghai struck on August 5, the dikes at Shitangkou outside Dongmen and Laoshidong in the Fifth District of the Baoshan Seawall were washed away by the flood tide, causing the bottom of the bank walls to loosen and collapse by about ten feet each. After hearing the news, the county government immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau to requisition labor on the spot and prepared more than 1,000 sacks to mix with pebbles, sand, and mud to rush to block the danger, and drove piles on the inner dike. Yesterday, a reporter from Dagong News Agency drove to the breach of the Baoshan County seawall to inspect. The project to block the breach of the dike has just been completed last week.

Provincial Officials Survey

After the Jiangsu Provincial Government received the emergency telegram from Zhang Mingjing, the county magistrate of the county, it ordered the Construction Department to handle it quickly. Now Zhao Daihua, the director of the Construction Department, has specially sent Chen Zhitian, a water conservancy engineer, to Shanghai to go to Baoshan and meet with Section Chief Qi of the Third Section of the county government. They have been surveying the situation of the seawall dikes on the main and branch dikes for days in order to report everything to the province.

Flood Prevention Funds

Now that the autumn flood season is approaching, the water level in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River has been rising sharply in recent days. Baoshan is the hub of the water flow of the East China Sea, the Yellow Sea, and the Yangtze River. The location is dangerous. Although the Jiangnan Seawall Engineering Office has built the dikes in recent years, the dikes are quite solid, but it is necessary to prevent the sea tide from erupting in advance. Therefore, the county has telegraphed the provincial government to quickly allocate funds for prevention in order to prevent future troubles. It is now learned that the funds will be allocated immediately after being approved by the provincial government meeting.

Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed the Ministry Requesting Exemption of Repeated Business Tax for Fujian Tea Merchants

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China, in order to request an order to exempt Fujian Province tea merchants from repeated business tax, submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: We recently received a letter from the Fuzhou Minhou Silk and Tea Trade Association, stating that the tea industry is crucial to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and cannot withstand repeated burdens. They earnestly request a detailed investigation and submission to the central government departments, with a clear order to the Fujian Provincial Government to swiftly abolish the special business tax on tea and handle the ordinary business tax for hongs according to regulations, in order to ensure fairness and save the tea industry. The case involves Bao Chong'an and Zheng Fuduan, representatives of the Maotea Public Guild Hengyuan Hall, and Sun Xi and Yang Renqi, representatives of the Guangfu Tea Guild Gongyi Hall, who stated that their guilds had previously requested that the Fuzhou Tea Industry Business Tax Bureau, upon order to reorganize the tea tax, establish an ordinary business tax for hongs. They petitioned at various levels, requesting permission to temporarily postpone the establishment of the general business tax before the special tax on tea was abolished, in order to avoid duplication and alleviate merchants' difficulties, which was already submitted on record. Now, they have received the Ministry of Finance's directive No. 10020 of the Fu character on July 8th, stating, 'The submission has been noted. Please consult the Fujian Provincial Government to investigate and comply accordingly.' This directive shows a desire to maintain [the industry], and we are extremely grateful. We should have waited quietly for compliance, without daring to trouble you further. However, in recent days, the personnel handling the business tax have intensified their efforts, urging payment more and more severely. They even sent letters to various hongs on August 4th, stating that the amount of business tax should be based on the amount of special tax already paid, and collected pro rata as the standard for levying ordinary business tax on hongs, requiring payment within three days, which is quite inappropriate. However, the business of the hongs is in a state of economic depression, and they have no desire for personal gain. Even if they stop business, they would not regret it. They only hope that the tea industry will consider the entire future, and they have deep concerns, so they cannot help but speak out. We believe that the tea industry in Fujian Province has recently declined dramatically, and the state of the disastrous defeat is truly pitiful. Examining the reasons, although it is due to foreign products occupying sales and blocked sales channels, the excessive burden and high cost are also factors in the failure. However, it is difficult to raise the price in the sales market, and if the burden is increased, the mountain base will inevitably be lowered, and the farmers' hard-earned income will not be enough to maintain their lives. Therefore, the abandonment of tea mountains is inevitable, and the impact is extremely significant. The government should have the necessity to help this serious social condition. We respectfully present our humble views again. (Omission) In general, hongs and tea merchants are originally integrated businesses, which is clearly different from the separate businesses of other tea firms and cannot be compared. Moreover, the special tax burden is already heavy, and since the order to abolish it has not been followed, the ordinary business tax for hongs is established again, which is actually a repeated levy. At this time of the disastrous defeat of the tea industry, it is already difficult to maintain it, so how can it be repeatedly levied? In addition to again presumptuously going to various agencies in the province to appeal, requesting that the ordinary business tax for hongs be postponed before the special business tax is abolished, if the ordinary business tax is to be implemented as ordered and cannot be stopped, then the business tax levied on special goods is respectfully requested to be abolished. In addition, we have stated the above reasons and requested the General Assembly to swiftly submit [this petition] to the Shanghai National Federation of Chambers of Commerce to uphold justice and submit it to the various departments of the National Government, requesting permission to issue a clear order to stop it, in order to alleviate the people's difficulties and alleviate merchants' hardships. According to this, after investigating the various points stated by the two guilds, they are indeed true, and it is reasonable to submit this presentation. We implore your esteemed association to investigate and approve this presentation to uphold justice and submit it to the Central Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry to issue a clear order to the Fujian Provincial Government to order the bureau to stop the repeated tea industry business tax, in order to preserve a glimmer of hope for the tea industry. We are deeply grateful. Respectfully, The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China." On this basis, we deem it appropriate to send a telegram to your esteemed ministry to respectfully request investigation and approval, requesting permission to consult the Fujian Provincial Government to stop the repeated tea industry business tax, in order to maintain the business of tea merchants, which is most earnestly prayed for. Sincerely, The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China.

Yu Qiaqing Urges the Ministry of Railways to Maintain Creditworthiness for the Shanghai-Zhejiang Railway Loan; Reduction of Principal and Exemption of Interest Impacts the Entire Domestic Debt; Plans to Accompany Bondholders to Petition the Ministry

Yu Qiaqing, a prominent figure in Shanghai, recently telegraphed the Ministry of Railways at the request of representatives from the Shanghai-Zhejiang Railway creditors, urging the Ministry to uphold its creditworthiness and allocate sufficient funds to cover both principal and interest. The telegram to Zhang, Minister of Railways in Nanjing, reads as follows: "Esteemed Minister Zhang, according to letters from Yang Qicheng, Yan Zhonglin, Wang Huaide, and other representatives of the Shanghai-Zhejiang Railway bondholders, the Ministry and liquidation office announced a reduction in principal and exemption of interest for the overdue final bond installments of the Shanghai-Zhejiang Railway. As their hard-earned money is at stake, they are unwilling to accept this unexpected loss and firmly oppose it. I, Yu Hede, was the signatory representing the nationalization of the railway and am requested to assist in advocating for their cause. In my opinion, the government invariably repays both principal and interest for foreign debts of Chinese railways, such as the Jinpu Railway, and even prepaid the outstanding British debt for this railway multiple times. However, for this overdue final bond installment, the government is reducing the principal and exempting the interest. This disparate treatment of domestic and foreign debts is unfair and will have a significant impact on the entire domestic debt market, which the government should avoid. I, Yu Hede, was the representative for the nationalization of the Zhejiang Railway. At the time, it was stipulated in the sale agreement that a branch line would be built from Yuyao to Longshan, but this has not been implemented for over twenty years, resulting in losses of over two million yuan for personal investments in Longshan Wharf and other facilities. This is a grave breach of trust by the nation towards its people. Now, to further reduce the principal and exempt the interest for this final bond installment is deeply regrettable. The bondholders have repeatedly come to me requesting redress, and I find myself unable to cope. Therefore, I plan to accompany the bondholders to your esteemed ministry to request full repayment of principal and interest. I am sending this telegram in advance, hoping you will investigate and swiftly order the preparation of sufficient funds to be available when we arrive to claim them, thereby maintaining creditworthiness. I eagerly await your reply. Sincerely, Yu Hede." He has already sent letters to each team and dispatched several external affairs officers to liaise with them to conclude the effort. It is reported that the results and receipts of each team are due to be submitted by the end of this month to facilitate the finalization and announcement.

Agricultural Loan Syndicate Reorganized as the Agricultural Capital Bureau's Working Capital Syndicate; Negotiations Completed with Thirty Participating Banks; Each Bank Underwrites Capital; Board of Directors Established to Preside

According to the Xin Sheng She, the Ministry of Industry's joint establishment of the Agricultural Capital Bureau is nearing completion and is about to open. The method of handling agricultural loans by the China Agricultural Loan Syndicate has also been agreed upon. The details are as follows:

Negotiating Reorganization

The Agricultural Capital Bureau has fixed capital allocated by the government, matching capital jointly underwritten by various banks, and working capital provided by a syndicate of banks. The fixed capital and matching capital for the 25th year of the Republic, each amounting to 6 million yuan, have been allocated by the government and underwritten by the banks. As for the working capital, Assistant Director Zou Bingwen has successfully negotiated with various banks to reorganize the China Agricultural Loan Syndicate into the Agricultural Capital Bureau's Working Capital Syndicate to handle agricultural loans. The reorganization will be announced upon the opening of the Agricultural Capital Bureau.

Participating Banks

The China Agricultural Loan Syndicate was established in the spring of the 24th year of the Republic. The initial participating banks were the Bank of Communications, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, Jin Cheng Bank, Continental Bank, Zhong Nan Bank, Kuo Hua Commercial & Savings Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, New China Bank, and the Farmers Bank of China, totaling ten banks. The syndicate's handling of agricultural loans proved quite effective. After the reorganization, in addition to the above ten banks, the Bank of China, Yien Yieh Commercial Bank, Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank, Jiangsu Bank, Sze Ming Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, The National Commercial Bank, China General Edison Company, China Merchants Bank, Chung Foo Union Bank, Ken Yeh Bank, The Farmers and Workers Bank of China, The Commercial Bank of China, Chuen Kung Bank, Tung Lai Bank, China & South Sea Bank, Post Office Savings Bureau, China First Trust Company, Central Savings Society, and Central Trust Bureau, totaling thirty banks, have joined.

Loan Procedures

The syndicate has decided to establish a board of directors to oversee agricultural lending. All participating banks will be directors. In addition to establishing a general office, regional offices will be established in agricultural areas of each province. At the beginning of each year, a board meeting will be held to determine the total amount of agricultural loans for each province and the loan recipients. All loans will be handled in accordance with the previous China Agricultural Loan Syndicate's procedures. Capital will be self-subscribed by each bank, with each unit being 50,000 yuan in national currency. The loans will primarily target major agricultural products such as rice, wheat, and cotton, focusing on production and marketing loans. In addition, there will be loans for the construction of agricultural warehouses in various provinces.

After the Smuggling Craze Started, Someone Conspired to Extort Minister Kong; Yan Jiezhi Was Trapped in the Hostel and Had Wild Ideas; Minister Kong Telegraphed Chairman Zhao Requesting to Handle It According to Law

According to Xin Sheng She, recently a major extortion case has been rumored in Shanxi, involving the Jin Feng Hou firm, which is managed by Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance. Yesterday, a reporter met a gentleman who had just come from Taiyuan and talked about the process as follows:

Minister Kong Has No Time to Take Care of It, Manager Is Responsible

Minister Kong is from Taigu County, Shanxi Province. Taigu values business, and the commercial forces are all over the world. During the early years when Kong was committed to the revolution, he also engaged in business according to the local customs, and the scope was very wide. In recent years, because he has been serving in the central government, he cannot take care of it. All the firm has been responsible for managing it. The firm established by Kong in Yuci County is called Jin Feng Hou. This firm annually manages sugar, and the wholesale quantity is huge.

Old Stored Sugar, Fabricated Accusations

According to past practice, the goods are imported at the end of the year and transported to Shaanxi and Gansu provinces in the spring and summer of the following year. This spring, the red bandits disturbed Shanxi Province, and the local area was unstable, so most of the sugar was old stocks, which had already been registered by the local chamber of commerce and transferred to the county government and court. Since the smuggling craze started, the customs has implemented anti-smuggling regulations. The informer can get huge bonuses for reporting smuggled goods. Therefore, the sugar stored in Jin Feng Hou has attracted the attention of the wicked, who think it is profitable. They fabricated the term smuggled goods and reported it to the Zhengtailu Police Bureau. The police sent the police to seize more than 2,000 pieces of sugar stored in the store as smuggled goods. It has now been handed over to the court for handling.

Wild Ideas, Letter Extorted Kong

After the news of the case reached the province, it happened that Yan Jieru, a fellow villager, was looking for work in the province. It had been several months since he had accumulated huge expenses for lodging and meals. He had a wild idea and sent a letter to Minister Kong, claiming that he knew a news reporter Liu Mou and learned that the Zhengtailu Bureau recently seized more than 2,000 pieces of smuggled sugar in Yuci, involving the Jin Feng Hou firm operated by Kong. The firm had been asking Minister Kong to intercede, and it was heard that the Shanxi Provincial authorities agreed to find a way to eliminate it secretly. It also said that Liu Mou intended to disclose this situation and had tried to prevent it. He asked how to deal with it. The implication was that he wanted to take this opportunity to extort Minister Kong, so as to solve his predicament in the province.

Kong Shixiang, Zhao Daiwen Fairly Investigate the Matter

It is reported that Minister Kong was shocked after receiving Yan's letter. Since he was far away in Beijing and Shanghai, he had no way of knowing the contents of the case. Even the Jin Feng Hou firm had never cleared customs, let alone intercede. He telegraphed Chairman Zhao of Shanxi Province, asking him to investigate thoroughly, and that if the firm had illegally transported goods, it should be investigated according to law. I will never defend him. After receiving the telegram, Chairman Zhao replied to Kong, saying that the case of the smuggled sugar seized in Yuci County had been handed over to the court for handling. The manager of Jin Feng Hou had not asked the provincial government to exempt him from investigation, and the provincial government had not tried to eliminate it secretly. Later, he received a telegram from Kong, saying that if it was found that there were illegal circumstances after the investigation, please handle it strictly in accordance with the law, and should not be lenient because the firm was operated by him. Now it is reported that Chairman Zhao deeply admired Minister Kong's selfless spirit and has informed the court to handle this case carefully and not to wrong or let go. It is not difficult to find out the truth. At the same time, Yan Jieru, who sent a letter to Kong to extort him, has also been summoned for handling. As for the reporter Liu mentioned by Yan, he has also been found to be non-existent. His intention to coerce and extort is more proof.
