Economic Supplement

A Humble Proposal for Reforming the Currency System of Guangdong Province

— Xu Deguang

(1) Introduction

The currency system of Guangdong Province has always been extremely complex and chaotic. Recently, due to the military's habit of using 20-cent subsidiary coins and subsidiary dollar notes as a medium of exchange, endless financial disputes have arisen. This is because the subsidiary dollar has not gained a position in foreign exchange, and its price often fluctuates. All market transactions use Hong Kong banknotes as the standard of payment, which makes the credibility of the Hong Kong dollar stronger and the foundation of the subsidiary dollar weaker. Changes in its price often affect industry, commerce, and all trades, and even involve the rural economy. Anyone familiar with the situation in Guangdong Province knows that the Hong Kong dollar actually controls the economic lifeline of the entire province. Even in normal times, Guangdong Province urgently needed to reform to a silver dollar standard. Since the central government implemented the legal tender policy last year, the Guangdong provincial authorities have taken the opportunity to issue banknotes arbitrarily. Initially, in November of last year, the Finance Department issued an order to centralize silver, stipulating that one silver subsidiary dollar would be exchanged for 1.2 subsidiary dollar notes, and one silver dollar would be exchanged for 1.44 subsidiary dollar notes, in an attempt to absorb a large amount of silver and make up for the emptiness of the treasury. At that time, the Finance Department's accumulated expenses were all paid in banknotes. After the changes in Guangdong and Guangxi, military expenditures inflated, and the number of banknotes issued arbitrarily was even more difficult to estimate. The price of banknotes plummeted, and the market panicked. All silver, except for that held by the Preparatory Custody Committee, was either hidden among the people or escaped to Hong Kong, almost creating an irreparable chaos. This is another reason why the Guangdong provincial banknotes urgently need to be reformed to a silver dollar standard due to the current pressing needs.

(2) The Problem of Reform

The central government's current reform of the currency system in Guangdong Province is based on the main principles of safeguarding the legal interests of the people of Guangdong Province and avoiding excessive burdens on the government. Therefore, we must first consider all aspects, adopt a gradual approach, and strive to achieve the goals of stabilizing finances and unifying the currency system within a certain period of time. The following points should be noted when drafting the plan:

(1) The issue of the amount of new legal tender to be issued.

(2) The issue of the exchange rate between the new legal tender and the subsidiary dollar notes.

(3) The relationship between creditors and debtors.

(3) The Reform Plan

There is no accurate public announcement of the amount of banknotes issued in Guangdong Province and its silver reserves. According to records, the total amount issued is 250 million yuan, and the cash reserve is equivalent to 10.7 million subsidiary dollars. The guarantee reserve includes more than 92 million yuan of provincial treasury bonds, but these treasury bonds currently have no market price or credibility, so it is difficult to consider them as reliable. Therefore, the first step of the reform plan must be to thoroughly examine the nature of the reserve and the amount of issuance as the criteria for determining the amount of new currency to be issued. However, referring to various records, the amount of banknotes issued in Guangdong Province is not far from the above number. Let us assume this number as the standard for formulating the reform plan.

(A) First-Step Plan

(1) Establish a Guangdong branch of the Central Bank to issue 120 million yuan of legal tender. The existing silver in Guangdong Province is worth a total of 10.7 million subsidiary dollars. Calculated at a discount of 20% to silver dollars (subsidiary dollars in Guangdong Province are complex and of varying fineness. If we calculate their pure silver content in terms of silver dollars, it would be difficult. Therefore, we propose to follow the market price of 12 subsidiary dollars in Shanghai being equivalent to one silver dollar), it is worth approximately 8.91 million yuan. Now we propose to issue 120 million yuan of legal tender in the first step. The cash reserve has reached more than 70%. The remaining 30% of the guarantee reserve can be supplemented with central government bonds. In this way, the foundation can be considered solid, and credibility will inevitably increase day by day.

(2) Stipulate that one silver dollar legal tender is equivalent to 1.6 subsidiary dollar notes, and gradually withdraw 192 million yuan of subsidiary dollar notes. The total amount of subsidiary dollar notes issued in Guangdong Province is 225 million yuan, and the cash reserve is approximately 10.7 million yuan. One subsidiary dollar note is only worth about 43% of its original silver content. If calculated at a 20% discount, it is only equivalent to 16% of a silver dollar. Now, at the rate of 1.6 yuan for one silver dollar legal tender, one subsidiary dollar note is equal to 63% of a silver dollar, which is 75% higher than the original stipulated price.

However, some may think that the 60% rate is too high, and the people of Guangdong Province will suffer excessive losses. It is not known that since the Finance Department promulgated the decree to purchase silver, the value of subsidiary dollar notes has fallen to 12% of its original value, which is approximately equal to 82% of a subsidiary dollar. At a 20% discount, it is only equal to 69.44% of a silver dollar. The proposed exchange rate between subsidiary dollar notes and silver dollar legal tender is 16 to 10, meaning one subsidiary dollar note is equivalent to 62.5% of a silver dollar. The actual price of subsidiary dollar notes after the reform is equal to 90% of the pre-reform price.

In fact, there is little difference. Given the disorder of the Guangdong provincial banknotes, and after the reform, such a result can be achieved, the people of Guangdong Province will be overjoyed even if they lose 10%, and they would not dare to disagree.

Some say that the exchange rate between subsidiary dollars and silver dollars in Guangdong Province is often around 30%, and the exchange rate for this reform should also be set at 20% to be fair. It is not known that the exchange rate between subsidiary dollars and silver dollars in Guangdong Province has often been between 35% and 40% in recent years. Even before this change in Guangdong Province, it often fluctuated between 28% and 41%. Now, let us assume it is 38%. Compared with the new currency system's 60%, the price is only 13.75% lower than the original. The calculation formula is as follows:

Conversely, if the ratio of subsidiary dollar notes to silver dollars is set at 3 to 10, the price of subsidiary dollar notes will be higher after the reform than before. This is not only unreasonable, but also enough to give speculators the opportunity to manipulate the market, and the central government would bear a heavy burden. Who would believe that this is a good plan?

In summary, if subsidiary dollar notes are gradually withdrawn at a rate of 60%, the losses of the people of Guangdong Province will not be excessive, and the central government will also be able to handle it with ease. This is a win-win situation.

(3) Stipulate the method of repaying debts with legal tender. Before the implementation of legal tender in Guangdong Province, subsidiary dollars and subsidiary dollar notes circulated equally. When the local authorities used the name of legal tender to engage in expansion, they stipulated that one subsidiary dollar was worth 1.2 subsidiary dollar legal tender notes. Therefore, a difference in price arose between subsidiary dollars and subsidiary dollar notes. On the one hand, the government used this method to absorb silver, and on the other hand, it stipulated that debtors could repay debts at face value with legal tender. The method was fundamentally contradictory. However, at that time, the government was eager to collect silver and had to use the premium method. On the other hand, because the price of legal tender and silver coins has always been equal, forcing debtors to pay an additional 20% would cause additional losses and inevitably lead to disputes. Conversely, when creditors lent money, except for a few exceptions, they all received and paid out in subsidiary dollar notes. Therefore, there were no losses on either side. However, the central government's current reform of the currency system in Guangdong Province is very different from that time. In recent months, the arbitrary issuance of subsidiary dollar notes has become more severe, and their purchasing power is vastly different from that before November of last year. After the new legal tender is issued, both subsidiary dollar notes and subsidiary dollars will be a kind of goods other than currency, and the prices must be differentiated to distinguish between different grades. By the same token, debts that occurred before November 3rd of last year cannot be compared with those that occurred after that date. Therefore, after the new currency system is implemented in Guangdong Province, at least the following four methods should be stipulated for repaying debts with legal tender:

(1) From the date of implementation of the new currency system, all company transactions, deposits, loans, tax payments, and debt repayments should be conducted in silver dollar legal tender.

(2) For all public and private debts that occurred before November 3, 1935, and whose contracts or regulations specify that they should be paid in silver subsidiary coins (i.e., subsidiary dollars): when repaid in silver dollar legal tender, the exchange rate should be set at one silver dollar legal tender being equivalent to 1.44 silver subsidiary dollars.

(3) For all public and private debts that occurred from November 3, 1935, and whose contracts or regulations specify that they should be paid in subsidiary dollar legal tender or have no stipulation, when repaid in silver dollar legal tender, the exchange rate should be set at one silver dollar legal tender being equivalent to 1.6 subsidiary dollar legal tender.

(4) For all public and private debts arising from lease, mandate, or employment relationships, unless otherwise agreed by both parties, regardless of whether the debt is continuing, the date of the contract shall be the date of occurrence of the debt.

(B) Second-Step Plan

(1) Issue 40 million yuan of Guangdong financial treasury bonds to absorb as many subsidiary dollar notes as possible. The amount of subsidiary dollar banknotes issued in Guangdong Province is 250 million yuan. In addition to the 192 million yuan exchanged for silver dollar legal tender, there are still 58 million yuan left. It is proposed to issue 40 million silver dollars of Guangdong financial treasury bonds to gradually withdraw the remaining notes at a rate of 60%. It is estimated that after deducting handling fees and discounts, 60 million yuan of subsidiary dollar notes can be absorbed. At this point, all subsidiary dollar notes will be eliminated, and the currency system will return to unity.

(2) Continue to issue 10 million yuan of silver dollars to purchase silver from the people. Six months after the new currency system is implemented, if the foundation has been stabilized, the issuance of legal tender can be continued with 30 million yuan to purchase silver from the people. It is estimated that there are still tens of millions of yuan of silver in the rural areas and major cities of Guangdong Province. If the issuance of legal tender continues, it can be absorbed as much as possible. The exchange rate can be set at one yuan of legal tender being equivalent to 1.2 yuan of silver subsidiary coins. After the silver is centralized, it will be used entirely as a legal tender reserve, and the credibility of the legal tender will become more consolidated.

(4) The Impact of the New Currency System on Various Aspects

(1) The Impact on Foreign Exchange: After the implementation of the new currency system, the national currency system will be unified, and the effectiveness of the legal tender policy will be able to be demonstrated in Guangdong Province at the same time. The foreign exchange rate in Guangdong Province will inevitably become more stable, unlike the erratic fluctuations of the past. The influence of Hong Kong banknotes will also gradually decrease, which is beyond doubt. Since the central government implemented the legal tender policy, the exchange rate between legal tender and Hong Kong dollars has often been around 91.5. In recent years, the exchange rate between subsidiary dollar notes and Hong Kong dollars in Guangdong Province, except for abnormal cases, has also often fluctuated between 15% and 50%. There is a great difference between them, and the risks borne by industrial and commercial operators are profound. After the reform, due to the stability of foreign exchange, Guangdong merchants will not only be able to avoid dangerous burdens, but also be able to directly purchase foreign exchange, eliminate the exploitation of foreign trading companies, and reduce various losses in exchange. This is all beneficial and without any harm.

(2) The Impact on Prices: After the implementation of the new currency system, once the foreign exchange rate is stable, the prices of foreign goods will inevitably become more stable, and the prices of local goods will increase due to the convenience of transportation between the north and the south, and the unification of the currency system, which makes circulation easier. As for the rise and fall of prices, there will be slight changes in the month or two before and after the reform, but after a certain period of time, they will inevitably return to normal. Now let's try an example to illustrate it. For example: Item A is produced in Shanghai, and Item B is produced in Guangzhou. The price of both items in Shanghai is one silver dollar, and the price of both items in Guangzhou is 1.4 subsidiary dollars. After the reform in Guangdong Province, the prices of both items in Guangzhou will rise to one silver dollar, equivalent to 1.6 subsidiary dollar notes. At first glance, prices seem to have risen, but in fact, the exchange ratio of the two items is still one to one, and merchants in Guangdong and Shanghai will not suffer any losses. However, general consumers (actually subsidiary dollar note holders) will inevitably lose 10% when they exchange 1.6 subsidiary dollar notes for one silver dollar legal tender. In fact, this kind of loss will ultimately be borne by the subsidiary dollar note holders, and has nothing to do with consumers. For those who rely on salaries, remuneration, and other income for their livelihoods, although the amount of their income is obviously different from before, their standard of living will remain unchanged, which is self-evident.

(3) The Impact on Industry, Commerce, and Finance: After the implementation of the new currency system, prices in Guangdong Province will gradually stabilize, and the foreign exchange rate will also tend to be stable. It will break the previously chaotic and irrecoverable situation, eliminate the risks of foreign trade, and investors will inevitably be enthusiastic. Financial activities and credit will develop, and industry and commerce will become increasingly prosperous. Tax revenues will become more abundant, and taxes will naturally increase. Moreover, the exhaustion of financial resources in Guangdong Province and the complexity of the currency system are actually one of the main reasons. After this reform, once the currency system is unified, it can reduce various losses in exchange and various twists and turns in revenue and expenditure. Revenue will not be reduced, and the government will be able to obtain endless convenience in financial administration.

(5) Conclusion

In summary, the current reform of the currency system in Guangdong Province is aimed at stabilizing prices, balancing foreign exchange, unifying the currency system, and regulating finance, which is a pressing need at present. As for the reform methods, the only principles should be to protect the legal interests of the people and reduce the government's burden. On the one hand, a reasonable amount of legal tender should be issued to meet current needs and gradually abolish subsidiary dollars. On the other hand, an appropriate exchange rate between subsidiary dollars and legal tender should be set to facilitate industrial and commercial transactions and resolve debt disputes. Finally, silver should be centralized as much as possible to completely eliminate subsidiary dollar notes and complete the unified legal tender policy of the country. These are just the broad outlines of the reform plan. As for the precise numbers and detailed methods, they can only be discussed after a considerable period of investigation and research.

— Written on August 20, 1936, at the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance —

The Key to Reorganizing Guangdong Currency

— Tan Bingwen

As the economy develops and commerce becomes more frequent, the need for stable money becomes increasingly urgent. This is because currency serves as a measure of value, and commercial transactions are merely transfers of value. However, the concept of "currency stability" evolves with the times. In the past, during the era of the free gold standard, it was generally believed that maintaining the weight and fineness of the currency metal was the key to currency stability. Before and after the European War, various countries issued banknotes excessively and without limit, leading to the advocacy of the reserve stabilization theory. At that time, exchange rates fluctuated greatly, and some scholars confused the stability of exchange rates with currency stability. The most advanced proponent of currency stability was Mr. Irving Fisher of the United States, who advocated that currency stability should be based on price stability, which has a significant and profound impact on the national economy. As for the fixed weight and fineness of currency metals and the stability of reserves, under the managed inconvertible paper standard, they have no foreign exchange significance; if they do, it is only a matter of psychological factors. If Gustav Cassel's purchasing power parity theory of currency is not flawed, then the exchange rate is merely a reflection of prices between two or more countries. Therefore, seeking exchange rate stability without price stability is like climbing a tree to catch fish and is certainly unattainable. Conversely, if prices are stable among all economic entities, then exchange rate stability will naturally follow.

When we study the issue of reorganizing the Guangdong currency system, we must also start from this point. Otherwise, a difference of a hair's breadth can lead to an error of a thousand miles, and the problem will be difficult to resolve correctly. Unifying issuance, establishing a Guangzhou branch of the central bank, and centralizing reserves are all technical issues that are not difficult to implement. The biggest difficulty today is the exchange rate between Guangdong currency and national currency, which requires theoretical exploration and practical alignment. Therefore, I will study the recent opinions of various experts and briefly express my own views for the reference of those in charge.

(1) Exchange Rate Dumping Theory

Here, I would like to first study Mr. Huang Yuanbin's theory, as Mr. Huang advocates for "currency stability." Mr. Huang strongly criticizes the stability of currency weight and fineness, as well as the stability of reserves, and his focus seems to be directly on the exchange rate. Regarding the exchange rate between Guangdong currency and national currency, he advocates that "the best rate is the average rate of the one or two weeks before implementation, fixed at a point between plus five and plus six." This argument is not without its flaws. Short-term fluctuations should only be regarded as abnormal changes. For example, last year, the exchange rate between Guangdong currency and national currency once rose to 90% or parity, while recently it has fallen to plus five or plus six, both of which are speculative phenomena. Mr. Huang's preference for plus five and plus six over 90% or parity is said to be due to a focus on the economic welfare of the people of Guangdong. He specifically pointed out: "From the perspective of production, trade, overseas remittances, and agriculture, industry, and commerce, the fixed rate should be low." This statement is rather vague. Upon closer examination, China's production industries rely heavily on the import of foreign machinery and raw materials, and a low exchange rate will increase production costs, which may not be competitive with imported goods. In terms of trade, suppressing the value of exports and encouraging imports may not be beneficial, and only extreme national economic theorists can deny this. The same reasoning can be applied to other aspects, which I will not elaborate on. In my opinion, Professor Huang's greatest theoretical errors are: (1) confusing the devaluation of Guangdong currency with the devaluation of national currency; (2) neglecting the price balance between Guangdong Province and other provinces. Because of the first error, Mr. Huang believes that the depreciation of Guangdong currency is equivalent to the depreciation of national currency, thus reaping the benefits of currency devaluation and dumping. This is the core of Mr. Huang's theory, which I therefore call the exchange rate dumping theory. However, we must understand that the devaluation of Guangdong currency does not necessarily achieve the effect of devaluation, but rather suffers the harm of devaluation first. Why? The implementation of the devaluation of Guangdong currency is aimed at the domestic market. After the devaluation, it will join the "National Currency Bloc (Chinese Dollar Bloc)." Whether the Guangdong economy can benefit from the devaluation depends on the direction of the national currency. If the national currency maintains its current exchange rate, then Guangdong Province will not gain any benefit. Conversely, if the Guangdong currency is fixed at plus two or three or even half, then it will join the "National Currency Group." If the national currency adopts a policy of devaluation (such as maintaining it at one shilling), then Guangdong Province can also benefit from the low currency value, like other provinces. In terms of currency flow, if the exchange rate is fixed at plus six (i.e., 60 cents of Guangdong currency equals one yuan of national currency), which is plus four compared to the normal period of plus two, then the property and income of the people of Guangdong will be reduced by one-quarter, and government tax revenue will also decrease by the same amount. Suffering harm before gaining benefit, is this not the case? Although Mr. Huang mentioned the trend of currency devaluation in various countries after the European War in his article, he does not know that this is only a means of exchange rate war between countries. Now, the issue of the exchange rate between Guangdong currency and national currency is aimed at the domestic market. Does Mr. Huang still not understand the severity of the chaos in domestic exchange rates and want to start an exchange rate war between domestic provinces? Furthermore, even the United Kingdom, which holds the reins of global finance after the European War, implemented a revaluation policy to restore the exchange rate to its former level, focusing on stabilizing domestic prices. At the same time, France, which devalued its currency by half, is still terrified today, and this lesson can be learned. Moreover, if the Guangdong currency is devalued today, and the national currency is devalued again in the future, the people of Guangdong will suffer double losses and their resentment will deepen. Mr. Huang's other error is neglecting the price balance between domestic provinces. Taking Shanghai and Guangdong as an example, the wholesale price index in Guangzhou in 1922 was 104, while in Shanghai it was 102. In November 1924 (the month the new currency policy was implemented), the price index in Guangzhou fell to 92.3, while the price index in Shanghai rose to 98.27, and in March it rose to 99.41. From this, it can be seen that the price index in Guangzhou is gradually balancing with Shanghai. Once the Guangdong currency is devalued by another 25%, as Mr. Huang advocates, then prices in Guangdong will be so cheap that they can be dumped to other provinces, disrupting the domestic economic balance. Mr. Huang is so addicted to the poison of exchange rate dumping that he cannot extricate himself.

(2) Reserve Stabilization Theory

This is the opinion of the Guangzhou branch of the Chinese Economic Society and its president, Mr. Li Zongtai. This school focuses on the solidity of reserves and bonds after the reform, which seems even more backward than the exchange rate dumping theory. Mr. Li and others argue that the current amount of paper currency in circulation in Guangdong Province is 249,212,062.50 yuan, and there is 10,745,000 yuan in silver (including 19,550,000 yuan in big dollars and 83,990,000 yuan in small dollars), totaling 67 million ounces of pure silver. If this silver is sold in New York at a price of 50 to 60 cents per ounce, it can be exchanged for 10 million US dollars, which is 12 million yuan in national currency. With this silver, another 10 million yuan in public bonds can be issued, which can issue 100 million yuan in national currency notes, meeting the regulation of four silver reserves to one note. Adding 30% to the 200 million yuan in national currency (which is Mr. Li's proposal), it can recover 250 million yuan in old currency, and the amount is not much different. Mr. Li also pointed out that issuing 80 million yuan in public bonds is easy, and there is no problem in terms of guarantee and acceptance. However, according to my observation, even if Mr. Li's method is used, calculated at a ratio of plus three, the current reserve is still insufficient by about 4 million yuan, which needs to be raised by those in charge, this is one point. I have no objection to issuing public bonds. However, in my humble opinion, even if the guarantee and acceptance aspects are not a problem, the payment of interest and principal must be carefully considered. If public bonds are used for productive enterprises, the burden of repaying principal and paying interest will fall on those enterprises. If public bonds are used for reorganizing finance, the burden will fall on the people, which is equivalent to increasing people's taxes. Moreover, since the government has already issued many public bonds, it can obtain sufficient public bonds for collateral by mortgaging those bonds, without the need to issue new bonds, this is the second point. The above is purely from a technical point of view. From a theoretical point of view, since the implementation of the new currency policy in November last year, China has actually adopted a managed currency standard. Issuing banknotes does not require strict adherence to the theory of "currency doctrine." The so-called currency doctrine believes that the amount of currency in circulation in a society must be restricted and advocates strict adherence to a fixed reserve as the basis. The promulgation of the British Peel's Act in 1844 was the first sign of victory for this theory. Later, various countries followed suit, and vulgar monetary scholars regarded it as the supreme principle. However, the evolution of monetary theory to this day has denied this theory as self-evident, and the theory of managed currency has taken its place. Proponents of managed currency advocate controlling the quantity and velocity of currency circulation so that it maintains a balance with the volume of commercial transactions, thereby stabilizing prices. Now that the country has adopted a managed currency system, there is no need to rigidly demand the certainty of reserves, but only to pay attention to the stability of prices. According to the estimates of the Guangdong Provincial Bureau of Investigation and Statistics, in the past sixty years, about 300 million yuan of silver has flowed into Guangdong Province. Since Guangdong implemented the policy of buying silver, it has only bought more than 80 million small dollars and more than 19 million big dollars, with more than 180 million yuan still hidden among the people. If our government implements the policy of nationalizing silver again, and can buy 180 million yuan, then it can continue to issue 200 million yuan of banknotes. If the government adopts this policy, then Guangdong paper currency will suddenly increase to more than 100%, which is a cause for concern. On the other hand, it is not easy to raise silver from the people, and the existing silver reserves are flowing out to compensate for overspending, thereby affecting the contraction of currency, which is also a cause for concern. It is believed that the note issuance reserve is only a psychological factor, like the window dressing of banks, which can be temporarily dealt with and should not be overemphasized. If we still adhere to the old concept and use the amount of reserves as the basis for note issuance, then it will not be successful and will lead to currency instability, as mentioned above, which is not the original intention of reserve stabilization.

(3) Raising Parity Theory

This is advocated by various industry associations in Guangzhou, and although the theory superficially advocates half exchange, its real purpose is to raise the value of Guangdong currency. The reason is roughly: "Although the announcement of buying silver at plus one was made last year, in fact, all merchants and people in the province, whether depositing money or transacting money, are returning to a certain amount of legal tender according to the original number of silver dollars. This amount is more than several times higher than the government's buying and selling. It can be seen that the merchants and people did not all get the benefit of exchanging legal tender at plus two. Now, if the legal tender obtained by exchanging silver dollars at parity must be exchanged for foreign dollars at a higher price, wouldn't it increase the people's losses?" -- Guangzhou Min Guor Daily, August 11, declaration by the City Chamber of Commerce. Here, the exchange rate issue can be divided into two discussions, one is the exchange rate between national currency and Guangdong banknotes, and the other is the exchange rate between Guangdong legal tender and Guangdong silver dollars. This article focuses on the issue of the exchange rate between Guangdong currency and national currency, because Guangdong legal tender and Guangdong silver dollars should be exchanged at parity, the reason is obvious, as mentioned above. As for those who advocate different exchange rates between national currency and Guangdong legal tender and Guangdong silver dollars (such as Li Yin'nan, see Bank Weekly, Volume 20, Issue 20), they only get the appearance and do not know the reality. However, the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce's theory can be used to explain that Guangdong legal tender and Guangdong silver dollars should be exchanged at parity, but not to explain that Guangdong legal tender and national currency should be exchanged at parity. Why? Because the exchange rate between Guangdong currency and national currency, in its normal state, originally revolved around plus two, and the parity theory advocates abolishing this plus two, which is equivalent to raising the value of Guangdong currency by 20%. The advantages and disadvantages of this theory are exactly the opposite of the exchange rate dumping theory. Although the nominal income of the people of Guangdong will increase as a result, and the national tax revenue will also benefit, industry and commerce will inevitably suffer from the harm of expensive currency. To put it more bluntly, those who advocate raising the currency value have not considered the risk of the collapse of the Guangdong economy.

The above three theories are inevitably biased and do not focus on managing currency and stabilizing currency. They only focus on the exchange rate issue, but if this issue is left to individual subjective judgment, it will not be easy to determine. For example, Mr. Huang Yuanbin, the director of the Department of Economics at Sun Yat-sen University in Guangzhou, has repeatedly changed his exchange rate proposals, sometimes advocating plus four and sometimes advocating plus five. There are even those who advocate using the old ratio of buying big dollars in Guangdong Province, plus 4.4, as the standard, boasting that it is based on facts, but in terms of reasoning, it is completely unfounded. Mr. Li Taichu's ratio of plus three, although similar to the arguments of those who advocate currency stabilization, is based on a wrong starting point. The parity theory also has considerable reasons, but it is regrettable to confuse the exchange of silver dollars with Guangdong banknotes at parity and the exchange of silver dollars with national currency at half. There are even those who advocate reorganizing the Guangdong currency system using the old method of reorganizing Sichuan paper currency, which is also due to a lack of understanding of the financial situation in Guangdong Province. At that time, the Sichuan issuance system had not yet been unified, so the central government promoted central paper currency in Sichuan Province, allowing it to form its own exchange rate, and gradually recovered the old Sichuan currency, avoiding the trouble of considering the exchange rates of various miscellaneous banknotes one by one. The situation in Guangdong Province is different. Since the Reserve Custody Committee has been established, the power to issue banknotes is entirely in the hands of the Bank of Guangdong, accounting for 240,722,065.50 yuan, while the City Bank only accounts for 8,500,000 yuan. In my opinion, suppressing or raising the value of Guangdong currency is not in the interest of the people of Guangdong. The path we should take is to stabilize the currency of Guangdong Province. I will try to state my views as follows.

(4) Currency Stabilization Theory

This theory can be obtained from the three principles of the Ministry of Finance for reorganizing the Guangdong currency system, which state: (1) to prevent the vast majority of people from suffering losses during the reorganization; (2) not to reduce tax revenue excessively; (3) to integrate Guangdong currency with the legal tender reserve. Next are the four items listed in the opinion of the Guangdong Provincial Legal Tender Issuance Reserve Custody Special Committee: (1) to settle silver to strengthen people's faith; (2) (3) to stabilize the exchange rate between big and small dollars, and to consider the economic interests of the majority of the people; (4) to expand and contract banknotes according to social needs. As a believer in currency stabilization, I also agree with this theory. In my opinion, it is appropriate to stabilize the ratio of big dollars to small dollars at plus 1.5. The reasons are as follows:

A. It is suitable for commercial habits and encourages production enterprises. In the past few years, the exchange rate between Guangdong small dollars and Shanghai currency has mostly revolved around plus two, and Shanghai currency is actually the representative of national currency. Now, this ratio of plus 2.5 is not only suitable for commercial habits, but also slightly higher than the normal state in the past, so it encourages production enterprises.

B. Government tax revenue is not affected. In the past twenty years, the Guangdong provincial tax revenue and the exchange rate of big dollars have been calculated at plus two, then plus 2.5, and plus two. Today, setting the ratio at 2.5 does not change much, and the government's tax revenue will not be lost. This is the second point.

C. Banknotes and reserves are financially sound. In terms of reserves, according to Mr. Li Taichu's theory, combined with the calculation method of plus 2.5, the amount of banknote issuance without reserves is only several million yuan. There is still a huge amount of 180 million yuan of silver hidden among the people, and it is not difficult to raise sufficient silver reserves. The silver reserve for banknote issuance by each issuing bank in Shanghai is always above 70%. If it is not easy to buy silver in Guangdong for a while, it can be temporarily supplied by Shanghai, which is also easy to do. However, we should pay attention to the fact that silver reserves only have a psychological effect at best, and although it cannot be completely ignored, there is no need to worry too much.

D. To prevent speculation between big and small dollars. After the ratio of big dollars and small dollars is fixed at plus 2.5, the exchange rate with small dollars in Shanghai and other places will be very close, so as to prevent speculative activities of small dollars. Otherwise, at the beginning of the implementation of the new system, the old auxiliary currency can still be circulated, and its price will inevitably have abnormal changes, which can be predicted.

E. After the Guangdong currency is stabilized at a ratio of plus 2.5, the internal economy of the people of Guangdong will not be affected at all. If the government wants to implement a national devaluation policy in the future, it will not cause resentment among the people of Guangdong.

F. Finally, from the procedural point of view, it is also quite consistent to decide the ratio of big dollars to small dollars at 102.5 to 100.

Parity is the ratio of the metals contained in two different currencies. If this currency reform adopts a ratio of plus 2.5, which is very close to parity, then there will be no loss for those who use silver dollars, so they will be happy to use big dollars (i.e., exchange silver dollars for big dollar bills), which will obviously help the promotion of big dollar bills. If the ratio is fixed at plus five or plus six, then those who hold silver dollars will naturally not be willing to exchange them for legal tender at a low price, and the trend of hoarding will inevitably arise.

The above classification is made by me from the perspective of monetary science for the convenience of research. And the final currency stabilization theory can take into account all aspects, which is not only in line with theory, but also in line with the actual situation, so I think this theory is more correct. However, those who advocate currency stabilization pay the most attention to price stability. After the exchange rate issue is resolved, efforts should be made to stabilize prices. The above-mentioned special committee, as the agency for compiling the price index in Guangzhou, should continue to compile it. If there are abnormal changes in prices or exchange rates after the new system is implemented, the amount of banknote issuance can be expanded or contracted at any time to adjust it. Last week, August 17th to 22nd, at the Huashang Securities Exchange, was the last week of futures trading for August. The trading resumed with two sessions each in the morning and afternoon. Therefore, the market did not experience a huge squeeze due to the proximity of delivery. Although the 96 government bond was raised to outside the ten yuan mark, it still failed to go straight up, which shows that rumors are not valuable and turned down greatly. Today is the last day of August, and it is still nothing more than a situation where swap transactions compete for gains and losses. Looking back on the past week, the environment was dull on Monday. The number 10 bond, which has always been short, suddenly went long, and the market price rose very sharply, by 45 cents to 90 cents, which was the best day of the week. The week was shrouded in swap transactions, and the market price was uneven. Category A alone fell, while the rest rose slightly. On Wednesday, due to the good situation, bulls came out, and the selling was very strong. Numbers 4 and 10 bonds all turned to selling, and fell back by half a yuan to 75 cents. On Thursday, the market was initially weak, but suddenly rose sharply at the close. There were also rumors in the market, and the market price actually rose by 12 cents to more than 70 cents. On Friday, there was suddenly a large amount of selling in the financial sector, and the market price was hit again, and the downward trend reappeared. Later, it recovered by 12 cents to 65 cents. On Saturday, short positions were covered, and swap transactions were not lively. The market price was firm, recovering by 12 cents to 56 cents. The market situation for the week fluctuated, which was controlled by swap transactions. It needs to wait until August is over before there will be greater changes. The results of the week's market price were slightly better, rising by 5 cents to 12 cents. Category B rose by 55 cents this month, which was the most. The 96 bond rose by 60 cents. Beginning of Studies on Folding Fans

— Ni Gaofeng

Cui Bao's "Notes on Ancient and Modern Times" states: "Shun made five-ming fans." This is the origin of fans, but their shape and method of production are no longer attainable. After the Han Dynasty, round fans were commonly used, made of fine silk, hence also known as silk fans. At that time, many poems praised round fans, the most famous being Ban Jieyu's "Song of Complaint," which contains the line, "Newly made fine Qi silk, round like the bright moon." Jiang Yan's poem contains the line, "The silk fan is like a round moon, coming from the loom." Thus, their shape and material were the same as those in vogue today, but there is no mention of folding fans. Folding fans can also be called "clustered-small fans" or "folding fans." The time of their origin is debated. According to the "Book of Southern Qi": "Chu Yuan used a waist fan to shield the sun." Hu Sanxing's note states: "Waist fans are worn at the waist, now called folding fans." This is the earliest appearance of the term "folding fan." Zhao Yanwei's "Yünlù Man Cao" states, "Folding fans use steamed bamboo as bones, lined with silk, and wealthy families sometimes use ivory for the head, decorated with gold and silver, probably originating from Goryeo." Lu Shen's "Spring Breeze Hall Notes" states, "Since the Southern Song Dynasty, many poems and lyrics have praised clustered-small fans. Su Dongpo mentioned a white pine fan from Goryeo, which, when opened, was more than a foot wide, and when closed, was only about two fingers thick, just like today's folding fans, suggesting that they already existed in the Northern Song Dynasty." It also says, "The Japanese made them with gold-painted surfaces and black bamboo bones as tribute." According to Zhao and Lu's accounts, folding fans already existed in the Song Dynasty, but one says they came from Goryeo, and the other says they were tribute from the Japanese, a slight difference. However, "Autumn Enclosure Miscellaneous Ornaments" claims: "During the Yuan Dynasty, Goryeo presented folding fans as tribute. During the Yongle period of the Ming Dynasty, they began to be popular in China. During the Xuande and Hongzhi periods, Li Zhao and Ma Dong were both famous for making fans." "Tianlu Kan Yu" also says: "Folding fans were anciently called clustered-small fans, held by servants, for convenient concealment in sleeves, to avoid the eyes of the noble. In the Yuan Dynasty, Goryeo began to present them as tribute. During the Yongle period of the Ming Dynasty, people began to imitate them slightly. Now they are becoming increasingly popular, and round fans are discarded." According to these two accounts, folding fans entered in the Yuan Dynasty from Goryeo, which differs from the previous two accounts. Generally, in the Song Dynasty, the Eastern Yi, Goryeo, occasionally presented folding fans as tribute, but they were not yet popular in China. By the Yuan Dynasty, those two countries presented them as tribute more frequently, so their popularity gradually increased domestically. By the Ming Dynasty, the Chinese were already imitating them themselves. This is a brief history of folding fans. Some say that clustered-small fans are different from folding fans, citing "Qu Tang Hua Ji," which states: "Folding fans are also round fans, which can be rolled and stretched, different from what is called clustered-small fans today." This is probably because there were no clustered-small fans during the Southern Qi Dynasty, and Hu Sanxing, in his commentary on the "Book of Qi," said that waist fans are today's folding fans, so he suspected that folding fans and clustered-small fans were different. However, round fans that can be rolled and stretched not only do not exist today, but there is also no mention of them in historical records, so his argument is ultimately unsubstantiated. As for Hu, who lived in the Yuan Dynasty, his commentary on the "Zizhi Tongjian," now called folding this and that, is using the present to explain the past, which is a common practice among annotators. Yan Shigu's commentary on the "Book of Han" has many such examples, so there is no need to be rigid about it.

The Standpoint of National Suicide

—

Half-Sheng Hall

— Guang Ji

Half-Sheng Hall is the name of a rich family's hall in our town. As for how it came to be called Half-Sheng Hall, that's quite a story.

The father of this rich family was a famous wealthy merchant, but when it was passed down to his son, because he had been spoiled since childhood, once he had power, he indulged in reckless prostitution and gambling, a life of luxury and dissipation. Limited money could not supply endless extravagance. In a few short years, the family fortune was squandered! After "everything was pawned" and "even porridge was unavailable," his father passed away due to illness! All that was left was half a sheng of rice that hadn't been eaten. When it was the turn of the rich man to take over, even though the "family circumstances were bleak," he was not discouraged or lazy. Instead, he was self-disciplined and frugal, taking the rice to the street to exchange for some sweets, taking them to the countryside to peddle, and then selling some local products from the countryside in the street, turning it over and over, earning a small profit. In this way, after a year or two, he accumulated several hundred yuan. Coincidentally, at this time, there was flooding, and the land along the embankment was available for cultivation. He used all the money to buy seeds and sowed them in the gaps. Fortunately, there was a bumper harvest that year, and he harvested a large amount of rice. Later, he also did some rice business, which went smoothly, so he created so many properties. Fearing that future generations would only know how to enjoy themselves and not understand the hardship of the ancestors' entrepreneurship, he named the hall Half-Sheng Hall to commemorate and show it to future generations.

I think this is right, because his descendants will be able to maintain the family fortune in the future.

Luan and Phoenix Exchanging Nests

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Five: Double Happiness Returns, Poems Inscribed on Leaves; Wedding Dress Tries on Luan, Tears Stain Silk Shawl

Therefore, although he tried his best to calm down and do his work as usual, he felt weak all over, as if he were sick, and he didn't know how to make himself comfortable. In desperation, he felt a little better only when he lay in bed. Therefore, he didn't read at night for two nights, and he also got up very late the next morning. On this morning, Liu Ma called outside the door: There's a registered letter. Please get up and stamp it. Guoqi thought it was the Shanghai Bookstore sending the royalties, so he quickly put on his clothes and got out of bed. He opened the door, stamped the letter, and took it. It was a thick envelope. The sender's address was written as Wu Siren, Danfeng Street, North of the City. He didn't have such a friend. When he opened the letter, it was a piece of white Xuan paper, with an eight-line note inside. This was a strange thing. He didn't have time to look at the eight-line note, so he held the Xuan paper up to the light. It turned out to be a green orchid, and the upper inscription was "For the Appreciation of Mr. Litian." The lower inscription was "Respectfully painted by the Master of Peilan Studio in late spring of the second year of the Republic of China." There was a quatrain on it: "Who will see you in the secluded valley? Spring comes, but you are alone. I have painted three or five leaves to send to a pure-hearted person." After Guoqi read it, he felt like a lottery winner who had won the jackpot, so happy that he wanted to jump up. He blurted out to himself: She agreed. So he put down the painting and immediately picked up the eight-line note to read. The few lines of writing on it were unusually delicate. The text was:

"To Mr. Litian's Esteemed Consideration: Upon receiving your second letter, I cannot help but feel anxious and ashamed. I told you before with utmost sincerity that my family rules are strict. The suspicion of melons and plums is only a small matter. Unexpectedly, long nights and short poems came one after another. Those who are like orchids in the ashes and dead wood cannot bear it, and it is more than just laughable. Sir, you are handsome and talented, and you are about to make friends with the people of the world and be famous among scholars. Why must you be so devoted to a weak woman who does not improve herself? I have painted a picture of orchid leaves to fill the blank space on your wall. This is not to repay your kindness, but to bid you farewell. With this memento, I should not fail to live up to your appreciation. I beg you to cherish your future and not send any more letters. I know my guilt, I know my guilt.

Respectfully, the Master of Peilan Studio, re拜 (bows twice)"

This was truly unexpected. The orchid painting was not a token of engagement, but a symbol of breaking off. After the gentleman finished reading the letter in one breath, he studied its meaning. She truly did not want to receive any more letters. However, she did not think that the letters he had written were offensive to her. From all aspects, she was a woman with both new knowledge and old morality. If he were to forgive her, it would be more appropriate not to write to her again. He took the letter and stood in the middle of the room, lost in thought. Liu Ma brought tea into the room, but he didn't even see it. His right hand held the stack of stationery, stroking it against the palm of his left hand. When Liu Ma called him twice, he finally woke up. He saw a pot of tea on the table and poured himself a cup. He picked up the cup, intending to drink, but felt his mouth was a little dry. This was because he hadn't washed his face or gargled yet. So he went to wash his face (page 64)

Special Feature

To the Country of "Midnight Sun" - Wang Jingqi Talks About Relations Between China, Sweden, and Norway

— Selfless

At 5 PM on August 18th, the red sun was high in the sky, and the weather was stiflingly hot. The Shanghai New Customs Wharf was crowded with people of all nationalities. Dozens of brightly colored flower baskets were displayed on the ferry. The newly appointed Minister to Sweden and Norway, Dr. Wang Jingqi, wearing a white serge suit and glasses, shook hands with each person who came to see him off at the wharf. He boarded the small customs ferry "Liping," and with the sound of the whistle, Minister Wang stood at the bow of the boat and waved goodbye as the senders waved their handkerchiefs and scarves. He boarded the German postal ship "Lanzino" and set sail for his new post at 8 AM on the 19th.

Sweden and Norway are two kingdoms in Northern Europe, located on the Scandinavian Peninsula, south of the Arctic Ocean and north of the Baltic Sea. Because the journey from China is far, Chinese people are relatively unfamiliar with the customs and political situation of these two countries. The reporter specifically inquired about this on the ferry, and Minister Wang kindly gave the following written statement:

Sweden and Norway were originally both vassal states of Denmark. At the beginning of the 16th century, Sweden broke away from Denmark and became independent, laying the foundation for the kingdom. In 1814, Norway separated from Denmark and also declared independence, but still recognized the Swedish monarch as its ruler, a kind of semi-independent state. It was not until 1905 that it declared its separation from Sweden and completed its independence. The division between Sweden and Norway has only been around for over thirty years.

"Sweden is an agricultural country, with a population of over six million, most of whom are farmers. Iron is the most abundant product. There are many forests in the country, and the timber and paper industries are also well-developed. The match trade is the world's best. Trade between China and Sweden began in 1847. The main imported goods to China are paper, copper, iron, and matches. The goods shipped from China to Sweden are tung oil, textiles, and antiques. According to customs statistics in 1935, the total value of Swedish imports was 8,587,284 yuan. The total value of exports to Sweden was 14,100,954 yuan.

Norway is a newly emerging industrialized country. The population is 2,810,000. The climate is extremely cold. Arable land accounts for only 4% of the total area, and habitable land accounts for only 75% of the total area. Fish is the main product. Before the European War, agriculture and forestry were relatively developed, but after the war, industry and commerce greatly declined. Imported goods from China include paper, cod liver oil, biscuits, milk powder, canned goods, and fish. Goods shipped from China to Norway include silk, silkworm cocoons, grains, tung oil, tea oil, duck feathers, and pig intestines. According to the 1935 customs report, the value of imports to China from Norway was 4,858,518 yuan. The value of exports to Norway was 604,801 yuan.

As for China's international relations with Sweden and Norway, in addition to the aforementioned trade situation, there is also cooperation in academic culture between China and Sweden. In recent years, Chinese and Swedish scientists have jointly formed the Northwest Scientific Expedition Team, cooperating with the Swedish Dr. Sven Hedin to collect various materials and specimens related to geology, meteorology, astronomy, humans, archaeology, and folklore, which will definitely contribute to science. Although there has not yet been such cooperation with Norway, the works of several famous Norwegian writers, such as Strindberg, Ibsen, and Bjørnson, have been translated into Chinese and have had a considerable impact on China's New Culture Movement."

Finally, Minister Wang told the reporter: "Because our people do not fully understand the situation in Sweden and Norway, they often regard the spectacle of the midnight sun in Northern Europe as an overseas oddity. This time, I am going to Sweden and Norway, and I will only uphold the government's intentions, strengthen friendly relations, and promote business and cultural endeavors. I would never dare to be greedy for the beautiful mountains and rivers of Northern Europe, and I only know how to serve the country. I am even more willing to introduce Chinese culture to the two countries of Northern Europe, so that the friendship between the two great nations of the East and West can be enhanced, and we can deeply understand each other."

Painted Stockings and Anklets

— Sun Linchang

Modern women, in the summer, are popularizing exposing their breasts and arms, baring their legs and feet, fully displaying their flesh. However, their legs are either yellow and thin or covered in scars. So they're now adding some kind of powder that used to be rubbed on their arms to their legs.

This year, they have added two new and novel ornaments—painted stockings and anklets. The so-called painted stockings are fake stockings painted on the legs, so the legs are completely bare, so that the painted ones resemble flesh-colored stockings. The painting method of this kind of fake stockings is very delicate. Its silk texture is exactly the same, and it is difficult to distinguish the real from the fake. It's just a pity that it cannot be washed. Because once it is exposed to water, the makeup will be washed away, returning to its original appearance.

Women's bare legs and feet have been popular for many years. This has indeed caused losses for sock factories. But businessmen are, after all, resourceful. In addition to providing nail polish to decorate their toes, this year they have invented a kind of gold anklet to decorate their calves. On the anklets, there are also several small bells that ring when they walk.

Inverted Consciousness

— Zhang Feng

A certain gentleman had just graduated from university and was about to go abroad to study. On the night before boarding the ship, at a public farewell banquet, he presented a beautiful booklet, asking those present to write some farewell messages.

The booklet was passed to a "vigorous and young" friend, who was about to pick up a pen to leave a message. Suddenly, he saw a horizontal line in the middle of all the words on the booklet and couldn't help but exclaim, "What's the meaning of this? Why scold people for being 'tired of not learning'?"

But in a moment, he also laughed with the crowd, because he immediately realized that he had been misunderstood by the habit of "writing Chinese like Western writing." It was originally a well-intentioned idiom: "Fond of learning and never tired"!

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao

Talk

Bai Chongxi

— Fang

The two problems currently facing the government that must be resolved as soon as possible are the North China issue externally and the Southwest issue internally. These two issues may not seem to be directly related, but the methods for resolving them are closely intertwined. The saying "the collapse of the Jin Mountains in the north will echo in Luoyang in the east" illustrates this point.

Regarding North China, after the Japanese Garrison Army convened a staff meeting a few days ago, military officials from Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, Shanxi, Shandong, and other provinces attended to discuss various North China issues. On one hand, negotiations on adjusting Sino-Japanese relations will begin once Kawagoe arrives in Beijing. The negotiation direction is still based on the three principles of Hirota. Although the details of the staff meeting and negotiations are not yet clear, the seriousness of the North China situation is undeniable.

Regarding the Southwest, since Chen Jitang stepped down, the Guangdong province is no longer a problem. However, recent news from Guangxi indicates that Li and Bai intend to consolidate their power and refuse to accept central government orders, which is regrettable. Li and Bai made significant contributions during the Northern Expedition, and recently their governance of Guangxi has also achieved considerable success. If Li and Bai could suddenly realize their errors and apply their spirit of governing Guangxi to Zhejiang, and their internal methods to external affairs, then their future contributions would surely surpass their contributions during the Northern Expedition. However, they persist in their errors, fighting like trapped beasts. I do not understand their intentions.

The reason why the central government has hesitated to use drastic measures against Li and Bai is precisely this. Therefore, they are willing to compromise and discuss the matter at length, hoping that Li and Bai will consider the overall situation and allow the Guangxi issue to be resolved peacefully. The extent of the central government's tolerance towards Guangxi is only this great. Now Li and Bai have been defiant for a long time, unwilling to change their minds, and ignoring telegrams of advice. Recently, there have been alarming reports of them forming a government and deploying strategies. If disaster strikes, everything will be destroyed. Even if Li and Bai do not consider their own lives and fortunes, do they not consider the general population of Guangxi? This attitude is truly incomprehensible.

While Li and Bai's contributions during the Northern Expedition and their achievements in governing Guangxi cannot be denied, their refusal to obey central government orders and come north is a sin that can be enumerated. Li and Bai cannot deny their guilt: first, the crime of undermining national unity; second, the crime of undermining domestic peace; third, the crime of undermining national spirit and solidarity; and fourth, the crime of undermining the diplomatic front and causing obstacles. Even if Li and Bai do not consider Guangxi, do they not consider the survival of the Chinese nation?

But Li and Bai say: I do not have time to consider anything. I would rather be a bandit, I would rather join the Communist Party, I do not care about any sacrifice, I do not care about any destruction. Is this foolish or evil? Unwilling to be a contributor to the Republic of China, but willing to be a sinner of the Republic of China. What is the reason for this? I cannot help but feel sorry for Li and Bai, and even more for my country.

Tofu Ah Wen

— Li Xuan

The tofu dregs in the bamboo basket are pressed on the wooden frame, dripping with milk-like soy milk.

It’s pitch black inside the house, with the sour smell of bean juice evaporating. White paste still drips drop by drop under the millstone, and the water bucket is almost full.

A big rat-like donkey pants, dragging the mill around and around on the wet ground. By the brick pool, in the bowl rack next to the mountain stove, a small Mobil lamp flickers. The small flame mixes with the smoke from the chimney, making the room dark like a coal mine.

"Ooh—wheeze," Ah Wen's wife arches her back at the stove to cook rice. The donkey stops to defecate, and she turns around and shouts.

The sky outside the window is getting dark, and the cold wind is still blowing, making the leaves laugh and roll.

Ah Wen carries an empty tofu peddler's pole, walking back to the alley from the street.

"Is the tofu all gone?" Wang the fat owner of the sesame cake shop greets Ah Wen with a smile, squinting his eyes.

"It's gone. Mr. Wang, have you eaten yet?"

"I have. Ah Wen, you're really working hard all day."

"Hey, how can you not suffer if you're living a poor life?" Ah Wen said and slowly walked out of the alley.

"How could someone like Ah Wen marry such a pretty wife?" Lin Er asks, holding an empty enamel basin, standing at the entrance of the barbershop.

The shoe repairman, nicknamed Bad Scraps, raises his head and laughs:

"A lazy man marries a beauty—Hey, Lin Er, do you know that someone wants Ah Wen's wife?"

"Don't even think about it, you can't touch her, what a joke!" Heh, Lin Er pushes open the wind door and walks in.

Mr. Wang touches the fat on his cheeks, his cracked mouth looks like a cotton peach: "They're a proper couple, what nonsense are you talking about!"

"Don't believe it, isn't this official's cousin Hu Yinsheng drinking soy milk there every morning?"

"They're doing business!"

"Isn't selling meat cakes business?"

"A dog's mouth can't spit out ivory!"

In the cool night, the third watch drum is beating in the alley, the tall poplar trees and the leaves are flying. The cries in the wind are a little desolate.

Ah Wen and his wife are sleeping soundly, the little donkey is eating grass in the shed, and the door is tightly closed.

"Bang...bang bang..."

Ah Wen's wife wakes up first, her heart beating.

"Wake up, listen, someone is knocking on the door."

Ah Wen rubs his eyes, turns over, puts on his cotton robe, and asks angrily:

"Who is it, in the middle of the night!"

"It's me, can't you hear? I'm Mr. Hu, from the Public Security Bureau..."

The door opens, a gust of cold wind crawls up Ah Wen's spine, he feels strange, Mr. Hu stumbles in, his butt bumping the door panel, his fist raised like a hammer:

"Ah Wen, don't shout, I want to discuss something with you."

Ah Wen feels like he's hit with a ball on his chest and his head is burning. He looks at the small foreign gun in Mr. Hu's hand.

"Mr. Hu, we poor people don't have money..."

"Bullshit, I want your money, you go out and find a place to sleep,"

Mr. Hu stares with bulging eyes, takes a breath, and takes out a silver dollar from his pocket "Take this, come back at dawn. Isn't it better than selling tofu?"

Ah Wen's chest only rises, like a small stone, a suffocating anger attacks his heart. His eyes glare, his dark face droops, his left arm rises to block, and the small foreign gun flies to the side of the tofu bucket.

"Fuck your mother, get out!" Ah Wen slams the door shut.

Mr. Hu massages his back, crawls up from under the house eaves, touching the injured spot that was kicked, and hobbles home in pain.

When the sun is peeking over the eastern mountain, small black crows are flying in the greyish white sky, the wind is cold and desolate, stray dogs run out of the alley, and the rooster has crowed three times.

Several policemen, wide awake from the cold, are running. Ah Wen is squeezed among them, his arms bound tightly behind his back.

"What law have I broken, officers!"

"Stop the nonsense!"

"Still pretending like nothing happened!"

"If you're timid, behave yourself, privately hoarding military firearms!"

Ah Wen lowers his head blankly, letting them carry him out of the alley. The shopkeeper of the oil and salt store wipes his eye boogers on the wooden door panel, and looks up for a while, saying:

"The tofu seller Ah Wen is in trouble!"

A vegetable peddler passes by and responds:

"I heard he's a traitor, has a gun, colluding with ×× people, don't know if it's true or false?"

Raft House

— Zhifu

Summer night, the bright moon hangs obliquely in the sky, and the river harbor is tranquil. The sound of water flows rhythmically. The footsteps on the embankment are relatively sparse at that time. The mosquitoes, however, become arrogant, gathering in the weeds, constantly stirring and destroying the calm air.

The water surface is peaceful. A row of wooden rafts is lined up on the left bank. Like a long snake, they lie lazily there. The raft house of the watchman, like a dragon's cub, is tied to the wooden raft, crouching and accompanying the quiet night.

Those trees, water plants... are reflected by the moonlight in the clear blue water, curling and rippling...

It is indistinguishable from which raft house this moving song comes from:—

"...In the second watch, the moon is east,

The moon is curved like a bow,

Shining on the poor man's raft house.

The poor man's fate is bitter!

The poor man's fate is locked in a cage.

For three meals a day, working for others.

Sweating and bleeding all year round,

Life cannot be relaxed at all...

When can we break free from the cage, break free from the cage!..."

The raftsman singing stretched his voice freely in the white night river harbor: seemingly intentionally sighing his own fate by the light of the bright moon.

The singing stopped for a while, and the air was silent again. Even the noises of those reptiles seem to be low. In the heart of the river, transparent white fog still spreads...

"Sun Lin!...Damn, monkey head! What are you learning from women's tunes,... it's simply... like a ghost crying!...Haha...it's simply..." Another bold voice rolled out from a raft house with a tin roof, sharply vibrating on the river harbor...

The raftsman Sun Lin, called the monkey head, sat leaning against the small window, staring blankly at the sky, as if he hadn't heard the drunken man's rude giant voice.

The sky is still flowing with bright white clouds, connected to the distant embankment and jungle, as if you can touch it with a single hand.

The raft house is filled with the smell of yellow wine, and the middle-aged raftsman He Geng is swallowing alone, moving his lips. This time, with seven points of drunkenness, he approached Sun Lin and slapped him heavily on the shoulder:

"What are you sad about?...Really like a monkey head pretending!...Okay! Let's be happy!...One day's work, damn!...Like cattle and horses...Look, when we get to the night, we like this little thing in the cup...Come! You and I drink a cup together..."

He grabbed Sun Lin's arm at random, entangled him fatefully. That uncomfortable smell of alcohol rushed out sharply from the wide mouth.

"Old Geng! Let you enjoy it alone! Greedy fellow...don't..."

Sun Lin frowned. He glared at him hatefully, broke free from Old Geng's grasp, lowered his eyes and looked at the swaying shadow in the river, watching it rise with an irregular curl and splashing apart...

"Monkey head!..."

A Geng flipped his eyelids and cursed heavily: Then, he rushed forward, preparing to reprimand him severely:

"Hey! Kid! Stop pretending, we...talking about fate,...the fate of us raftsmen,...is to suffer this lifetime...Which one is lucky?..."

Sun Lin was a little depressed. He suppressed his breath, unable to think of what words to argue with. He looked at the water shadow, then turned his eyes to look at the sky, and finally lowered his face again...

This time—Ah Geng finished muttering, and seemed to be a little sober from the alcohol, and his brain returned to its original state as usual, sympathizing, and looking at the sky with Sun Lin, his red and swollen eyelids tightly closed.

"Eh! We raft people sell our labor, what luck are we talking about!...My old partner!..."

There was no more sound to follow, and the raft house was silent.

Summer night, the bright moon hangs in the sky, floating clouds push in the sky, and the river harbor is still not quiet...

Afterthoughts

The "Coffee Bi-Monthly" published by Coffee Publishing House, edited by Zhao Chao and Chen Yaoting, is a beautiful illustrated magazine encompassing everything. It is a 16-open book with a color cover, specializing in exciting news from the film, dance, and broadcasting industries, and also features lively and vivid cartoons and photographs. Not a single page or article is unlovable. The publication is scheduled for September 1st, priced at one dime. For trial reading, please attach eight cents for postage and send it to Xing Zheng, Radio Station, Li Shude Hall, 250 Baker Road, Shanghai. It will be sent to you immediately after publication.

The folk music harmonica team organized by Yanyan Society has already started broadcasting. It is said that the organization is actively preparing, and will also be able to broadcast in the near future.

Movie

Special Feature

When filming the scene of You Guanren's drunkenness in "Little Sisters," You, in order to make the performance realistic, secretly drank several cups of sorghum liquor. Therefore, when filming began, he was already drunk, and the drunken scene thus achieved unexpectedly satisfactory results.

For the needs of the plot, "Little Sisters" inserted a scene of Ye Wenhuo emerging from a bath, which was both sensual and aesthetically pleasing.

Paris Refreshment Temporarily Suspends Screening

The Paris Theater on Avenue Joffre has always been known as the leader among the theaters in western Shanghai. In order to strive for perfection, the theater has spared no expense and has undergone a major renovation, replacing it with a new type of projector and installing a truly scientific silver screen. Therefore, starting today (the 24th), it will temporarily suspend screenings for three days. After that, the Paris Theater will be as perfect as it can be, and can be used as the best recreational place for Shanghai residents. It is also heard that the theater has signed long-term contracts with major film companies in Shanghai, such as MGM, Paramount, Warner Bros., Universal, 20th Century Fox, and Columbia Pictures, to show any blockbuster movies in the second or third round, to satisfy your eyes. The opening film has been selected as Paramount's "Barbary Coast," a second-run film starring Herbert Marshall, the lead actor in "Waterloo Bridge," leading six major stars to work together on a great structure. The showtimes have also been changed to: 1:30, 5:00, 7:00, and 9:15, with prices remaining the same. The theater will meet with all Shanghai residents on the 27th of the month.

Ronald Colman and Claudette Colbert co-star

A scene from "Under Two Flags"

Coming Soon to Grand Cathay

"Begonia Red" and "Women's Rights"

After producing "Peach Blossom After the Robbery," Zhang Shichuan successively produced two new films, one is "Begonia Red" and the other is "Women's Rights."

Zhang Shichuan's works rarely have delicate and fragmented descriptions. He always grasps the core of the play and completes his work in a bold manner. The story is narrated concisely and clearly, and the climax of the play is often very clearly presented. Sometimes he also appropriately adds some jokes. This is the superiority of his works.

"Begonia Red" is a performance that exhausts all joys and sorrows, sweet and bitter experiences. The story contains a very complex group of characters: a cowardly actress, a cruel child-exchanger, a licentious warlord and his sycophantic, manipulative henchmen, a kind and useless merchant, a heartbroken old man, a family of gentlemen, children searching for their mother, a loyal old servant... There are tears, there are smiles, there is anger, there is madness, there are sighs, there is ridicule, there are cries!

"Women's Rights" focuses on depicting the story of a woman, an intellectual woman who jumps out of the powdered and perfumed life circle of a young mistress. She begins to use her education to cultivate the barren land of society, but "love," a kind of thing, relentlessly besieges her. The so-called "women's status" is merely a vase in society. She begins to wander painfully everywhere, from the south of the Yangtze River to the northern country. She cannot enter society at all. At the end of the play, she still flees to the vast wilderness for "love."

Zhang Shichuan produced both scripts one by one. These two scripts, which obviously have a very distant distinction in meaning, are equally suitable for Zhang Shichuan's handling. Have you ever felt this way? He is very good at handling complex and intricate stories, with large-scale depictions. Both films are close to this kind of movie.

"Measure Talent Drama Journal" Inaugural Issue Published

The Liangcai Amateur Theater Troupe has been established for three months, and its internal work is thriving. In the past, it has performed two plays, "The Home in the Northeast" and "Echo," which have been well received by the audience. Now, "Measure Talent Drama Journal" is published. The printing is clear and the content is rich. The inaugural issue was published on August 20th. The content of this issue includes: Drama Movement and National Liberation, Director and Actor, Three Points to Note for Beginner Actors, We Still Need to Gather! (One-Act Play Script) and recent news about drama additions, etc. All theater lovers are welcome to subscribe. Please send letters to: the Teaching Affairs Office of Liangcai School, 3rd Floor, Continental Market, Shanghai, and attach one and a half cents of postage (limited to half a cent), and you will get a copy of the journal.
